The Number of Prophets: General Belief Over Specific Count
The author affirms general belief in the number of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the correct Islamic position on the number of prophets is general belief (iman ijmaili) rather than commitment to a specific number.

Core Idea
The number of prophets is known only to Allah – we believe generally.

This lesson examines the proper Islamic stance on the number of prophets. While some scholars have suggested 124,000, the majority view is that we should not commit to a specific count due to lack of definitive evidence. The Quran itself indicates that many prophets are not mentioned to us, so our faith should be general.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the verse citation and the reference to Al-Nasafi.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage mentions two positions: some scholars specified 124,000, but the author rejects committing to any number. Understand why.
3
Understand the evidence
The author cites lack of proof from Quran or Sunnah and quotes the verse 'and messengers We have not mentioned to you.' See how this supports general belief.
4
Grasp the caution from Al-Nasafi
Al-Nasafi warned that specifying a number risks including false prophets or excluding real ones. This reinforces the wisdom of general belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا ، فلا بد أن يكون عدد الأنبياء على مرّ العصور قد تجاوز الآلاف وقد حدد بعض العلماء عددهم بـ ١٢٤ ألفاً . ولكنا لا نرى كما قال جمهور العلماء - دليلاً من كتاب أو سنة أو أثر صحيح متبع يحملنا على التزام تحديدهم بهذا العدد أو بغيره . بل إن التزام ما جاء به القرآن والتأدب بأدبه يقتضينا أن نلتزم في ذلك جانب الإيمان الإجمالي تحقيقاً لمقتضى قوله عز وجل : ﴿ وَرُسُلاً لَمْ نَقْصُصْهُمْ عليك كم . ولا يُؤمنُ في ذكر العدد - كما قال النسفي - أن يُدخل فيهم من ليس منهم أو يُخرج منهم من هو فيهم (۱)
And on this basis, the number of prophets throughout the ages must have exceeded thousands, and some scholars specified their number as 124,000. But we do not see, as the majority of scholars said, a proof from the Book, the Sunnah, or a sound authoritative report that obliges us to commit to this number or any other. Rather, commitment to what the Quran brought and decorum with its etiquette require us to adhere in that matter to general belief, fulfilling the requirement of His statement, Exalted is He: 'And messengers We have not mentioned to you.' And it is not safe in mentioning the number—as Al-Nasafi said—that some who are not among them might be included or some who are among them might be excluded.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage deals with the number of prophets. The author states that the total number must be in the thousands, and some scholars specified 124,000. However, he argues that there is no definitive evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, or authentic reports that obligates accepting that specific number. Instead, the proper approach is to believe generally in all prophets, as the Quran says 'and messengers We have not mentioned to you.' He cites Al-Nasafi's caution: specifying a number risks including those who are not prophets or excluding those who are. Therefore, we should not commit to a particular count.

Key Terms
عدد الأنبياء
إيمان إجمالي
النسفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think we must know the exact number of prophets.
Correction: The correct position is general belief without specifying a number, as no definitive evidence exists.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject specifying the number of prophets as 124,000?
A) Because the Quran explicitly denies it.
B) Because there is no definitive proof from revelation requiring that number.
C) Because the number is actually higher.
D) Because only Muslims can be prophets.

Key Takeaway
The correct belief about the number of prophets is general belief, not a specific count.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content to believe generally in the number of prophets, or do you feel a restless need to know the exact count? Why does your heart seek certainty through details rather than trusting Allah's knowledge?
?
When you encounter a hadith or statement about the number of prophets, do you accept it without verifying its authenticity? How does this lesson change your approach to such reports?
?
Do you ever find yourself trying to know things that Allah has deliberately not revealed? How can you train your soul to be satisfied with the Quran's etiquette of general belief, even when your mind craves specifics?

The Prophet's Five Special Gifts and Universal Mission
The author quotes a hadith listing five special gifts granted to Prophet Muhammad, emphasizing his universal mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five special gifts granted to Prophet Muhammad that distinguished him from previous prophets, especially his universal mission to all humanity.

Core Idea
Muhammad's message is for all peoples, not just one nation.

The author highlights one of the most significant distinctions of Prophet Muhammad: his mission to all of humanity. To illustrate this, he quotes a famous hadith in which the Prophet enumerates five unique gifts granted to him. This passage establishes the universal scope of Islam and the special privileges bestowed on its final prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the Prophet's own words come through before interpreting.
The hadith is sahih (authentic), narrated by Muslim and Bukhari.
2
Identify the five gifts
List the five gifts in the order mentioned. Notice that the first gift (universal mission) is the most emphasized in this context.
The gifts are: 1) universal mission, 2) spoils made lawful, 3) earth as a mosque, 4) support by fear, 5) intercession.
3
Understand 'every red and black'
This phrase means all people of every race and color. It underscores that the Prophet was sent to all humanity, not just a specific tribe or nation.
4
Connect to the lesson's theme
Reflect on how this distinction (universal mission) is the third of several differences between the prophethood of Muhammad and previous prophets, as the author is explaining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - من أهم مظاهر الفرق بين نبوة نبينا محمد والأنبياء السابقين أن سيدنا محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام بعث إلى الناس كافة ، كما قال في الحديث الصحيح الذي رواه مسلم : « أعطيت خمساً لم يعطهن أحد قبلي : كان كل نبي يبعث إلى قومه خاصة وبعثت إلى كل أحمر وأسود ، وأحلت لي الغنائم ولم تُحلَّ لأحد قبلي وجعلت لي الأرض طيبة طهوراً ومسجداً فأيها رجل أدركته الصلاة صلى حيث كان ، ونُصرت بالرعب بين يدي مسيرة شهر ، وأعطيت الشفاعة » (۱) رواه مسلم في باب المساجد ورواه البخاري في باب التيم والمساجد
3. Among the most important aspects of the difference between the prophethood of our Prophet Muhammad and the previous prophets is that our master Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, was sent to all people, as is stated in the authentic hadith narrated by Muslim: 'I have been given five things that were not given to anyone before me: every prophet was sent specifically to his own people, but I have been sent to every red and black; spoils of war were made lawful for me and were not lawful for anyone before me; the earth was made for me pure and a mosque, so wherever a man from my community is overtaken by prayer, he may pray there; I have been supported by fear (striking into enemies) a month's journey ahead; and I have been given intercession.' Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Mosques and narrated by Al-Bukhari in the Book of Tayammum and Mosques.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage lists the third major distinction of Prophet Muhammad: his universal mission. The author quotes a hadith from Muslim where the Prophet enumerates five special gifts. First, previous prophets were sent to their own people only, but Muhammad was sent to all humanity ('every red and black' means all races). Second, spoils of war were made lawful for him. Third, the earth is made pure and a mosque, allowing prayer anywhere. Fourth, he was granted divine support by terror striking enemies a month's journey away. Fifth, he was given the right of intercession on Judgment Day. The footnote confirms the hadith's sources in Bukhari and Muslim.

Key Terms
بعثة عامة
خمس
الشفاعة
الرعب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Muhammad's message was only for Arabs
Correction: The hadith explicitly states he was sent to 'every red and black,' meaning all races and peoples, confirming the universal scope of his prophethood.

Checkpoint
What is the first special gift mentioned in the hadith?
A) The earth was made a mosque.
B) Spoil was made lawful.
C) The prophet was sent to all people.
D) Intercession was granted.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the five gifts underscores that Prophet Muhammad was sent to all humanity, unlike previous prophets who were sent only to their own people.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly see Islam as a message for all people, including those different from you, or do you subconsciously limit it to your own community? What step will you take this week to demonstrate that belief?
?
The Prophet was given the gift of intercession. Do you live as if you need his intercession? What has changed in your actions today because of that need?
?
The earth was made a mosque for you. When was the last time you prayed in a place you felt uncomfortable, recognizing that the whole earth is a place of worship for you? Challenge yourself to do that this week.

The Unity of Prophethood
The author asserts prophethood as one reality and prohibits differentiation between prophets in that essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophethood is one indivisible reality shared by all prophets, and that we must not differentiate between them in that essence.

Core Idea
Prophethood is one reality, not subject to variation between prophets.

This lesson establishes a foundational principle in Islamic theology: the unity of prophethood. Before we explore differences in rank or virtues among prophets, we must first affirm that the very office of prophethood is identical for all. The author grounds this in clear Quranic and prophetic statements, warning against any form of discrimination in this core reality.

Guided Path
1
Understand the key claim
Read the passage and notice that the author begins by stating that prophethood is a single reality. This is the central thesis. Ask yourself: what does 'single reality' imply about the nature of prophethood?
It implies that the essential relation to Allah is identical for every prophet.
2
Examine the prohibition
The author concludes that differentiation is not permissible in this respect. Reflect on what exactly is prohibited: not all forms of distinction, but only distinction in the prophethood itself.
This nuance preserves room for acknowledging differences in rank.
3
Study the Quranic evidence
Read the verse from Al-Baqarah (2:285) closely. Notice that the believers declare they make no distinction between any of Allah's messengers. This directly supports the author's point.
The verse affirms unity of belief in all messengers.
4
Study the hadith evidence
The author cites a hadith where the Prophet himself commands not to prefer him over Moses or other prophets. Consider why the Prophet would say this despite his own lofty status.
This teaches humility and reinforces the unity of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينبغي أن تعلم أن النبوة التي أكرم الله بها الأنبياء ، حقيقة واحدة ، لا تتفاوت ولا تختلف ما بين نبي وآخر . فلا يجوز التفريق بين نبوة نبي وآخر من هذه الناحية . وهو المقصود بقوله جل جلاله : ﴿ آمَنَ الرَّسُولُ بِمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ رَبِّهِ وَالمُؤْمِنونَ . كُلِّ آمَنَ باللهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ ، لا نُفَرِّقَ بينَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رسله ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٨٥] . وهو المقصود بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لا تخيروني على موسى ، ولا تفضلوني على الأنبياء
You should know that prophethood, with which God honored the prophets, is a single reality; it does not vary nor differ from one prophet to another. So it is not permissible to differentiate between the prophethood of one prophet and another in this respect. And that is what is meant by His statement, Exalted is His Majesty: 'The Messenger has believed in what was revealed to him from his Lord, and the believers. All have believed in God, His angels, His books, and His messengers, saying, "We make no distinction between any of His messengers"' [Al-Baqarah 2:285]. And that is what is meant by his statement, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Do not prefer me over Moses, and do not favor me over the prophets.'
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage explains that prophethood as a divine gift is one reality shared by all prophets; it does not vary in its essence. Therefore, we must not differentiate between prophets in terms of their prophethood itself. The author cites Quran 2:285, where believers declare they make no distinction between any of God's messengers. He also cites a hadith where the Prophet says not to prefer him over Moses or favor him over other prophets. This teaches humility and the unity of the prophetic office, though the author will later discuss superiority in rank as a separate matter.

Key Terms
النبوة
حقيقة واحدة
لا نفرق بين أحد من رسله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the prohibition implies that all prophets are equal in every way, including rank and virtue.
Correction: The passage only prohibits differentiation in the essence of prophethood, not in other aspects like rank, miracles, or virtues. Other texts establish relative superiority.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'لا نُفَرِّقَ بينَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رسله' primarily indicate?
A) We should not discriminate among prophets in terms of their prophethood.
B) All prophets are equal in every aspect.
C) We should not follow any prophet except Muhammad.
D) Prophets are not human.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is one indivisible reality; believing in that unity is essential, even if prophets differ in rank and blessings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the prophethood of Muhammad (saw) is the same in essence as that of Moses (as)? Examine your heart: is there any hidden feeling that your Prophet's prophethood is more 'real' because you were born into this ummah? If you internalize this unity, what would change in your attitude towards other religions?
?
The hadith commands us not to prefer Muhammad over Moses. In your daily conversations, do you ever speak about other prophets with less reverence? Think of a recent instance. What will you do tomorrow to actively honor the prophethood of all prophets equally?
?
If prophethood is one reality, then rejecting any prophet is rejecting the very institution of prophethood. How does this affect your commitment to believing in prophets you know little about? What step can you take this week to learn about a prophet you have not studied before?

Superiority of Prophet Muhammad in Rank
The author affirms the unique rank of Prophet Muhammad with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis for the unanimous consensus that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation in rank.

Core Idea
Prophet Muhammad is the best of creation because his mission is universal.

This passage addresses the rank of Prophet Muhammad among all prophets and creation. While prophethood is a shared dignity, the Prophet holds a unique supreme position. The author explains the reason and supports it with clear evidence from the Prophet's own words and the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation to get the literal meaning. Notice the author's claim and the two pieces of evidence.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بقطع النظر عن معنى النبوة'.
2
Understand the qualification
Note that the author separates rank from the shared prophethood. This clarifies that superiority is about rank, not the office of prophethood itself.
3
Examine the two proofs
The first proof is the Prophet's own saying, and the second is the Quranic verse about the best nation. Reflect on how the verse supports the claim.
The goodness of the nation depends on the goodness of its Prophet.
4
Address the misconception
Some think this contradicts the command not to differentiate between prophets. The author's distinction between rank and office resolves this.
The common misunderstanding is that it violates equality, but it's about rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما من حيث المنزلة - بقطع النظر عن معنى النبوة التي هي قدر مشترك بين الجميع - فلا ريب أن أفضل الخلق على الإطلاق هو نبينا م وهو مما أجمع عليه المسلمون قاطبة ، وذلك لعموم بعثته إلى الناس كلهم ، وفي بيان ذلك يقول عليه الصلاة والسلام : « أنا أكرم الأولين والآخرين على الله ولا فخر » وفي بيان ذلك يقول الله عز وجل : ﴿ كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ للنَّاسِ ﴾ [ آل عمران : ١١٠ ] إذ لا شك أن خيرية هذه الأمة تابعة لخيرية نبيها صلى الله
As for rank—aside from the meaning of prophethood which is a common denominator among all—there is no doubt that the best of creation absolutely is our Prophet Muhammad, and this is a point on which all Muslims have unanimously agreed. And that is due to the universality of his mission to all people. In explanation of this, he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'I am the most honored of the first and the last in God's sight, and I do not boast.' And in explanation of this, God Almighty says: 'You are the best nation produced for mankind' [Al-Imran 3:110], for there is no doubt that the goodness of this nation is dependent on the goodness of its Prophet, may God bless him [and grant him peace].
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage clarifies that while prophethood itself is a shared reality, Prophet Muhammad holds the highest rank among all creation. The author states this is a matter of unanimous consensus among Muslims. The reason is his universal mission to all people. He supports this with two proofs: the Prophet's own saying that he is the most honored in God's sight, and the Quranic verse calling the Muslim community the best nation, which derives its excellence from the excellence of the Prophet.

Key Terms
المنزلة
أفضل الخلق
خير أمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming Prophet Muhammad's superiority violates the Islamic teaching not to differentiate between prophets.
Correction: The passage clarifies that superiority is in rank, not in the essence of prophethood, which is shared. The command not to differentiate refers to accepting all prophets equally, not denying degrees of rank.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for Prophet Muhammad's superiority over other prophets?
A) He was sent to all mankind.
B) He performed more miracles.
C) He had more wives.
D) He lived later in history.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad is the best of creation because his prophetic mission is universal to all people, as affirmed by consensus, his own statement, and the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the fact that Prophet Muhammad's superiority is based on his universal mission challenge your own tendencies to restrict Allah's mercy to your own group? What would it mean for you to embrace the universal scope of his message today?
?
If Prophet Muhammad is the most honored of all creation, why do you sometimes give greater weight to your own reputation or the opinions of people than to following him? What one specific change can you make today to prioritize his honor over your own?
?
The passage says the ummah's goodness is dependent on the Prophet's goodness. In what area of your life are you relying on your own efforts rather than deriving your worth from your connection to him? Write down one concrete action that reflects that you are part of his best nation.

Belief in the Scriptures: General and Detailed
Author explains general and specific belief in scriptures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic principle of believing in all revealed scriptures, both generally for unknown ones and specifically for known ones.

Core Idea
We believe in all divine books, generally for the unknown, specifically for the known.

Muslims are required to believe in all scriptures sent by Allah to His messengers. But what about books we have never heard of? The author explains that our belief has two levels: general and specific. This passage clarifies that principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two categories of belief: general and specific.
The author uses the terms 'إجمالاً' and 'تفصيلاً'.
2
Distinguish general vs specific belief
Identify what is meant by general belief (believing without knowing details) and specific belief (believing with knowledge of names and attributes).
General belief applies to scriptures not named in the Quran; specific belief applies to those that are named.
3
Apply to known scriptures
List the scriptures mentioned in the passage: Torah, Gospel, Psalms, and the scrolls of Abraham. Understand that we believe in them specifically.
This includes affirming their original revelation, even if the current versions have alterations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لابد من الإيمان بالكتب التي بعث الرسل بها إلى أقوامهم وجماعاتهم لا نؤمن بها إجمالاً ، بالنسبة لما لم يأت فيه تفصيل وذكر أسماء . ونؤمن بها تفصيلاً بالنسبة لما ورد تفصيل في شأنه كالتوراة والإنجيل والزبور والصحف التي أنزلت على بعض الرسل كإبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام
It is necessary to believe in the books that the messengers were sent with to their peoples and communities. We believe in them generally with respect to what has no detail and no mention of names. And we believe in them specifically with respect to what has detail concerning it, like the Torah, the Gospel, the Psalms, and the scrolls that were revealed to some messengers, like Abraham, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage outlines the Islamic position on belief in scriptures. Muslims must believe in all books sent with prophets. For those that are not named or detailed in revelation, we believe generally (إجمالاً). For those that are named and described, such as the Torah, Gospel, Psalms, and the scrolls of Abraham, we believe specifically (تفصيلاً), affirming their names and attributes. This principle balances between what is known and unknown from divine revelation.

Key Terms
الكتب
إيمان إجمالي
إيمان تفصيلي
التوراة
الإنجيل
الزبور
الصحف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Muslims only need to believe in the Quran and reject all previous scriptures.
Correction: This passage clarifies that we must believe in all scriptures sent with prophets, both generally and specifically.

Checkpoint
How do we believe in scriptures that are not named in the Quran?
A) We deny their existence.
B) We believe in them generally (إجمالاً).
C) We consider them corrupted so we don't believe.
D) We only believe if they are mentioned by name.

Key Takeaway
Muslims believe in all divine books, generally for those not mentioned and specifically for those named in the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You routinely say 'I believe in all the books' in your declaration of faith. But have you ever actually pondered what it means to believe in the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms as revelations from Allah? Do you feel a connection to those earlier prophets and their communities, or are they just abstract concepts? Write down one specific thing you can do this week to honor that belief.
?
The passage distinguishes between general and specific belief. In your own life, do you tend to hold vague, general beliefs about Islam without seeking detailed knowledge? Where in your faith are you content with 'general belief' when Allah requires 'specific belief'? What is one area you need to investigate more deeply?
?
Consider that you will be asked about your belief in these scriptures on the Day of Judgment. Do you truly believe that the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms were revealed from Allah, or do you harbor doubts because of their current corrupted state? How does your belief in the original revelations affect your view of Jews and Christians today? This week, find one ayah that confirms your belief and reflect on it until it settles in your heart.

The Abrogation of Previous Laws and Scholarly Disagreement
The author states the clear abrogation rule and presents the scholarly disagreement on silent rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basic principle of abrogation in Islamic law and the scholarly disagreement regarding unmentioned previous rulings.

Core Idea
When the Qur’an and Sunnah speak, they abrogate the past; when they are silent, scholars differ.

This passage addresses a key issue in Islamic legal theory: how does the mission of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) relate to previous divine laws? The author explains that when the Qur’an or Sunnah provides a new ruling, it clearly abrogates the earlier ruling. However, for previous rulings that are not mentioned, scholars of usul al-fiqh disagree. Some consider them binding unless abrogated, while others hold that the mere mission of Muhammad abrogates all prior laws. This lesson examines that foundational disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's own wording introduce the concepts.
2
Identify the two categories of rulings
Notice how the author distinguishes between rulings that the Qur'an or Sunnah explicitly address, and previous rulings that are not mentioned.
3
Understand the two scholarly opinions
The passage presents two opinions: some say the law of those before us remains binding unless abrogated; others say it is abrogated by Muhammad's mission. Reflect on the difference.
This disagreement is a classic debate in usul al-fiqh.
4
Reflect on the scope of the discussion
The author notes that this issue belongs to usul al-fiqh and does not elaborate further. Why might he choose to only mention it briefly?
This shows the author's focus on creedal matters, not legal details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه الحقيقة واضحة لا غبار عليها فيما يتعلق بالمسائل والأمور التي عرض الكتاب أو عرضت السنة لحكم جديد لها ، فهو ناسخ لما كان من قبله . أما المسائل والأحكام السابقة التي لم يأت من الكتاب أو السنة أي بحث فيها ، فقد وقع الخلاف فيه عند علماء التشريع. فبعضهم قال : إن شرع من قبلنا يعتبر شرعاً لنا ما لم يرد ما ينسخه ، والبعض قال : هو ليس شرعاً لنا مطلقاً ، إذ إن مجرد بعثة محمد يعتبر نسخاً لمجموع الشرائع السابقة
ومكان تحقيق هذه المسألة علم أصول الفقه . فلا نطيل البحث فيها هنا
ولك أن تقول : ( الشرائع السماوية ) ، لتعددها واختلافها
ولك أن تقول : ( الأديان السماوية ) لعدم تعددها أو تخالفها ، إلا إذا أطلقت الدين على الشريعة مجازاً .
أما شريعة سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فلا ينسخها أي شرع ، إذ لا عبرة بالشرع إلا إذا كان وحياً من الله عز وجل ، وقد ثبت أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم هو خاتم الأنبياء ، فلا يتصور مجيء أي شرع ناسخ له
ثم إن شريعة نبينا ما فيها - كما تعلم ـ ما قد نسخ بعضه بعضاً لحكم باهرة لا مجال لشرحها هنا ، ومكان تفصيل الأمر في ذلك في علم أصول الفقه
And this truth is clear, with no doubt about it, regarding the matters and issues for which the Book or the Sunnah presented a new ruling, for it is abrogative of what was before it. As for the previous issues and rulings for which no discussion came from the Book or the Sunnah, there is disagreement among the scholars of legislation. Some of them said: Indeed, the law of those before us is considered a law for us as long as nothing comes to abrogate it. And some said: It is not a law for us at all, since the mere mission of Muhammad is considered an abrogation of the totality of previous laws. And the place for investigating this issue is the science of uṣūl al-fiqh. So we will not prolong the discussion of it here. And you may say: 'heavenly laws' (al-sharāʾiʿ al-samāwiyya), due to their multiplicity and difference. And you may say: 'heavenly religions' (al-adyān al-samāwiyya), due to their lack of multiplicity or difference, unless religion is applied to law metaphorically. As for the law of our master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, no law can abrogate it, for a law is only considered if it is revelation from Allah, and it has been established that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is the Seal of the Prophets, so it is inconceivable that any abrogating law should come. Then the law of our Prophet contains—as you know—what abrogates some parts of it for profound reasons, which there is no room to explain here, and the place for detailing that matter is in the science of uṣūl al-fiqh.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on abrogation and clarifies scholarly differences. The author states that when the Qur'an or Sunnah explicitly provides a new ruling for a matter, that ruling clearly abrogates whatever was before it. However, for previous rulings that are not mentioned in the Qur'an or Sunnah, scholars of legislation disagree. Some hold that the law of those before us (sharʿ man qablanā) remains binding for us unless a specific abrogation appears. Others hold that it is not binding for us at all, because the mere mission of Muhammad (peace be upon him) is considered an abrogation of all previous laws collectively. The author notes that this issue is properly investigated in uṣūl al-fiqh and will not be detailed here. He then makes a terminological point: one may speak of 'heavenly laws' (al-sharāʾiʿ al-samāwiyya) because they are many and differ, but one may also speak of 'heavenly religions' (al-adyān al-samāwiyya) because they are essentially one religion (monotheism) and do not differ, unless the term 'religion' is used metaphorically for law. Finally, the author emphasizes that the law of Muhammad cannot be abrogated by any subsequent law, because a valid law must come from Allah, and it is established that Muhammad is the Seal of the Prophets, so no abrogating law can appear. He also notes that within Muhammad's own law, some rulings abrogate others for profound reasons, but that subject belongs to uṣūl al-fiqh.

Key Terms
نسخ
شرع من قبلنا
أصول الفقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all previous laws are automatically abrogated by the mere mission of Muhammad, without considering scholarly disagreement.
Correction: The author shows that scholars differ: some hold that previous laws remain binding unless specifically abrogated, while others hold that Muhammad's mission abrogates them collectively.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the status of previous rulings that are not mentioned in the Qur'an or Sunnah?
A) They are definitively abrogated by Muhammad's mission alone.
B) They are all binding without exception.
C) Scholars disagree: some consider them binding unless abrogated, others consider them abrogated by Muhammad's mission.
D) They are part of Islamic law but optional.

Key Takeaway
The abrogation of previous laws is clear only when the Qur'an or Sunnah explicitly addresses a matter; otherwise, scholars hold two different opinions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a clear ruling from the Qur'an or Sunnah that contradicts a habit or previous understanding, do you immediately submit or do you resist? What does your reaction reveal about your faith in revelation?
?
How do you personally handle matters about which the Qur'an and Sunnah are silent? Do you seek knowledge to see if scholars consider it a valid difference, or do you follow your own opinion?
?
This lesson shows that even the silence of revelation can be a source of scholarly disagreement. How does that challenge your desire for certainty? Are you willing to live with ambiguity in matters of religion while continuing to learn?

Terminological Distinction and the Eternal Validity of Muhammad's Law
The author explains terminological options and asserts the eternal validity of Muhammad's law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between 'heavenly laws' and 'heavenly religions', and why the law of Muhammad cannot be abrogated.

Core Idea
Heavenly laws are many and differ; heavenly religion is one. Muhammad’s law is final, for he is the Seal of the Prophets.

In this passage, the author makes a subtle terminological point: we may speak of 'heavenly laws' (al-sharāʾiʿ al-samāwiyya) because they are multiple and differ in rulings, or we may speak of 'heavenly religions' (al-adyān al-samāwiyya) because they share the same core monotheistic belief. He then turns to the finality of Prophet Muhammad’s law, asserting that no subsequent law can abrogate it, since Muhammad is the seal of the prophets. This lesson explores these concepts and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the shift from terminology to finality.
2
Understand the terminological choice
The author says you may say 'heavenly laws' because they are multiple and differ, or 'heavenly religions' because they are one in essence. Reflect on this nuance.
The choice depends on whether you emphasize diversity of rulings or unity of belief.
3
Grasp the argument for finality
The author argues that Muhammad's law cannot be abrogated because he is the seal of the prophets, so no subsequent revelation is possible.
This is a creedal cornerstone.
4
Note internal abrogation
Within Muhammad's law, some rulings abrogate others for profound reasons, but that is a matter for usul al-fiqh.

Abrogation and the Status of Previous Laws
States the abrogation principle and presents the two scholarly opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly positions on whether previous divine laws are binding for Muslims after the advent of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Muhammad's mission itself may abrogate all previous laws, but scholars differ on unaddressed rulings.

Before we can discuss the finality of Muhammad's Sharia, we need to clarify a foundational debate in Islamic legal theory: what happens to earlier divine rulings after a new prophet comes? The passage begins by stating a clear principle about abrogation and then presents two contrasting views among scholars. Let's read it carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle of abrogation
Start by reading the first sentence: if the Quran or Sunnah brings a new ruling for a matter, it abrogates what came before. This is the basic rule.
Notice that this covers rulings explicitly addressed in revelation.
2
Identify the scholarly disagreement
Next, the passage addresses rulings not discussed in the Quran or Sunnah. There are two opinions: some say they remain binding unless abrogated, others say they are entirely abrogated by Muhammad's mission.
This disagreement is the core of the lesson.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how each position affects the way Muslims view previous scriptures. Which view seems more dominant? The passage does not pick a side here.
The author refers the detailed discussion to usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتاب أو عرضت السنة لحكم جديد لها ، فهو ناسخ لما كان من قبله . أما المسائل والأحكام السابقة التي لم يأت من الكتاب أو السنة أي بحث فيها ، فقد وقع الخلاف فيه عند علماء التشريع. فبعضهم قال : إن شرع من قبلنا يعتبر شرعاً لنا ما لم يرد ما ينسخه ، والبعض قال : هو ليس شرعاً لنا مطلقاً ، إذ إن مجرد بعثة محمد يعتبر نسخاً لمجموع الشرائع السابقة. ومكان تحقيق هذه المسألة علم أصول الفقه . فلا نطيل البحث فيها هنا. فهناك أن تقول : ( الشرائع السماوية ) ، لتعددها واختلافها. وقد يقال : ( الأديان السماوية ) لعدم تعددها أو تخالفها ، إلا إذا [؟] أطلقت الدين على الشريعة مجازاً . أما شريعة سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فلا ينسخها أي شرع ، إذ لا عبرة بالشرع إلا إذا كان وحياً من الله عز وجل ، وقد ثبت أن رسول الله هو خاتم الأنبياء ، فلا يتصور مجيء أي شرع ناسخ له. ثم إن شريعة نبينا ما فيها - كما تعلم ـ ما قد نسخ بعضه بعضاً لحكم باهرة لا مجال لشرحها هنا ، ومكان تفصيل الأمر في ذلك في علم أصول الفقه.
If the Book or the Sunnah presents a new ruling for a matter, it is an abrogator of what came before it. As for previous issues and rulings that were not discussed in the Book or the Sunnah at all, there is disagreement among scholars of legislation. Some said: The law of those before us is a law for us as long as nothing abrogates it. Others said: It is absolutely not a law for us, because the mere sending of Muhammad is considered an abrogation of all previous laws. The place to investigate this issue is the science of usul al-fiqh. So we will not prolong the discussion here. There you may say: 'heavenly laws' due to their multiplicity and difference. And one may say: 'heavenly religions' due to their singularity or conformity, unless one metaphorically applies 'religion' to law. As for the Sharia of our master Muhammad (peace be upon him), no law abrogates it, because a law is only valid if it is revelation from Allah Almighty, and it has been established that the Messenger of Allah is the seal of the prophets, so it is inconceivable that any abrogating law could come. Furthermore, the Sharia of our Prophet contains—as you know—that some parts abrogate others due to profound wisdoms that cannot be explained here, and the detailed treatment of this matter is in usul al-fiqh.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage discusses the status of previous divine laws after the advent of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and the principle of abrogation (naskh). The author begins by stating a general principle: if the Quran or Sunnah presents a new ruling for a matter, that new ruling abrogates what came before. Then he addresses the case of earlier rulings that are not mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah: scholars differ. Some say those earlier rulings are binding unless abrogated, others say they are not binding because Muhammad's mission itself abrogates all previous laws. The author notes that the proper place for this discussion is usul al-fiqh, so he will not elaborate. He then clarifies a nuance about terminology: 'heavenly laws' (shara'i') can be spoken of in the plural due to differences, while 'heavenly religions' (adyan) is singular in essence; using 'religion' for 'law' is metaphorical. The key point follows: Muhammad's Sharia cannot be abrogated because it is from Allah, and Muhammad is the seal of the prophets. The author also notes that within Muhammad's Sharia there is abrogation of earlier rulings by later ones, but that is a separate matter for usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
نسخ
شرع من قبلنا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that all previous divine laws automatically remain binding unless explicitly abrogated by a new text.
Correction: Scholars hold two views: some agree, but others say that the mission of a new prophet (like Muhammad) itself abrogates all previous laws, so unaddressed rulings are not binding.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of previous divine rulings that are not mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah?
A) They are automatically abrogated by Muhammad's mission.
B) They remain binding unless individually abrogated.
C) Scholars disagree: some say binding unless abrogated, others say abrogated entirely.
D) They are only binding for Jews and Christians.

Key Takeaway
The binding nature of previous divine laws for Muslims is contested: some uphold them unless abrogated, while others see Muhammad's prophethood as a universal abrogation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the mere sending of Muhammad abrogates all previous laws, what does that mean for how you view the Quran and Sunnah as your sole source of guidance? Do you truly submit to that authority, or do you still rely on other sources?
?
The author notes that the detailed discussion belongs in usul al-fiqh. Are you willing to study the principles that underpin Islamic law, or do you take rulings at face value? What might that reveal about your commitment to understanding your faith?
?
The scholars disagreed on whether unaddressed previous rulings apply to us. How does this disagreement affect your humility when learning fiqh? Are you quick to assume you know the ruling without respecting the scholarly process?

Finality of Muhammad's Sharia and Terminology
Clarifies terminology and affirms the absolute finality of Muhammad's Sharia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Muhammad's Sharia cannot be abrogated and the subtle distinction between 'heavenly laws' and 'heavenly religions'.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the seal of prophets, so his Sharia is eternally final and unrepealable.

After clarifying the disagreement on previous laws, the passage shifts to a crucial point: the absolute finality of Muhammad's Sharia. It also clears up a potential confusion in terminology—why we say 'heavenly laws' in the plural but 'heavenly religion' in the singular. This lesson will help you grasp the logical and theological basis for the permanence of Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Examine the terminology clarification
Read the lines about 'heavenly laws' (shara'i') and 'heavenly religions' (adyan). Understand why the plural is used for laws but not for religion.
The distinction is subtle: laws differ, but religion is one in essence.
2
Study the argument for finality
Next, the author argues that Muhammad's Sharia cannot be abrogated because he is the seal of prophets. No new revelation can come after him.
This is a logical proof based on the established fact of prophethood's finality.
3
Note the internal abrogation remark
The passage briefly mentions that within Muhammad's Sharia, some rulings abrogate others. This is an internal mechanism, not affecting finality.
This shows the Sharia is self-contained and dynamically complete.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that even after Muhammad, new divine laws could appear to modify or replace Islamic rulings.

Checkpoint
Why can Muhammad's Sharia not be abrogated according to the passage?
A) Because the Quran says so explicitly.
B) Because Muhammad was the most perfect prophet.
C) Because Muhammad is the seal of the prophets, and no divine revelation comes after him.
D) Because earlier prophets agreed to let Muhammad's Sharia supersede theirs.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's Sharia is absolutely final because he is the last prophet; internal abrogation exists but does not affect its status as the ultimate law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if Muhammad's Sharia is the final and complete guidance for all aspects of your life, or do you still look to other sources for moral direction? Are there areas where you prefer man-made systems over Allah's law? What will you change today to submit fully to the final Sharia?
?
The passage says no law can abrogate Muhammad's Sharia because he is the seal of prophets. Do you treat the Quran and Sunnah as the ultimate authority in your daily decisions, or do you sometimes prioritize culture, personal preference, or convenience? What would it look like for you to truly surrender to this final revelation?
?
The author mentions internal abrogation for profound wisdoms. Have you ever questioned why some earlier rulings were replaced? Does this shake your trust in the finality of the Sharia? How can you strengthen your conviction that Allah's wisdom is perfect even when you don't fully understand?

Masculinity as an Essential Attribute of Prophets
Defines masculinity as a necessary condition for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why masculinity is considered an essential attribute of prophets in Islamic theology and how apparent counterexamples from the Quran are interpreted.

Core Idea
Prophets must be male because perfection (kamal) is incompatible with femininity.

This lesson examines the first of the four essential attributes of prophets: masculinity. The author argues that prophethood is exclusive to males based on both historical precedent and theological perfection. He also addresses two Quranic passages that might seem to suggest otherwise, clarifying the meaning of 'wahy' in those contexts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage silently, then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the structure: definition, evidence, and refutation.
2
Understand the main evidence
The author provides two proofs: the historical reality that all prophets were male, and the attribute of perfection that is incompatible with femininity. Identify these in the text.
The consensus of Muslim scholars is also cited.
3
Analyze the counterexamples
The author mentions the mothers of Moses and Jesus, where the word 'wahy' is used. Consider how he explains these: the 'wahy' to Moses' mother is inspiration (ilham), and the command to Mary is an angelic call, not prophethood.
See the reference to bees as another example of 'wahy' meaning inspiration.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about why this attribute matters in Islamic theology. How does it affect the understanding of prophethood and the role of women?
This lesson shows the careful interpretation of Quranic language to maintain doctrinal consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثا
الصفات الضرورية للانبياء
ونقصد بصفاتهم ما يشمل شرائط النبوة التي يجب أن تتوفر فيهم كما يعبر بذلك أكثر علماء الكلام إذ الصفات الضرورية والشرائط شيء واحد لا فرق بينهما .
وجملة ما يجب للأنبياء أربع صفات
الصفة الأولى : الذكورة :
فلا تكون النبوة والرسالة لأنثى ، واعلم أن دليلنا على ذلك هو كل من الواقع الذي دل عليه إخبار الله تعالى عن الرسل والأنبياء الذين بعثهم إلى الناس على مر الزمن ، وصفة الكمال التي يجب توفرها للرسل والأنبياء ، وهي تنافي الأنوثة كما هو معلوم ، ولم يقع خلاف عند جمهور المسلمين في اشتراط هذه الصفة
واعلم أنه لا يتنافى مع هذه الحقيقة ، إسناد الوحي في القرآن إلى أم موسى في مثل قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَأَوْحَيْنَا إلى أُمّ موسى أن أرضعيه ... [ القصص : ٧] الآية ، ولا يتنافى معها أيضاً إسناد الأمر الإلهي إلى أم عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام في قوله جل جلاله : ﴿ فَناداها مِنْ تَحْتِها ألا تَحْزَني ... ﴾ [مريم : ٢٤ ] .
إذ الوحي المسند إلى أم موسى إنما هو بمعنى الإلهام ، وهو قدر مشترك للناس كلهم ، وقد أسند الله الوحي إلى النحل ، فقال : ﴿ وَأَوْحَى رَبُّكَ إِلى النَّحْل أَن اتَّخِذي مِنَ الجبال بيوتاً وَمنَ الشَّجَر ومِمّا يَعْرُشون ﴾ [النحل : ٦٨ ] والأمر المتجه إلى أم عيسى قد يكون نداء ملك مثل جبريل ، وهو بمجرده لا يعني النبوة ولا يستلزمها .
Third: The Essential Attributes of the Prophets
By their attributes we mean what includes the conditions of prophethood that must be present in them, as most kalam scholars express it, for the essential attributes and the conditions are one and the same, no difference between them.
The total of what is necessary for the prophets is four attributes.
The first attribute: masculinity:
Thus prophethood and messengership cannot be for a female. Know that our evidence for that is both the reality indicated by Allah's reports about the messengers and prophets He sent to people throughout time, and the attribute of perfection that must be present in messengers and prophets, which is incompatible with femininity as is known. There is no disagreement among the majority of Muslims regarding the requirement of this attribute.
Know that it does not contradict this fact the ascription of revelation (wahy) in the Quran to the mother of Moses, as in His statement: 'And We inspired (awhayna) to the mother of Moses: 'Suckle him...' [al-Qasas:7]—the verse—nor does it contradict it the ascription of the divine command to the mother of Jesus, peace be upon him, in His statement, Majestic is His Majesty: 'Then he called out to her from beneath her: 'Do not grieve...' [Maryam:24].
For the revelation (wahy) attributed to the mother of Moses is only in the sense of inspiration (ilham), which is a common share for all people. Allah has attributed revelation (wahy) to the bees, saying: 'And your Lord inspired (awha) to the bees: 'Take for yourselves among the mountains houses...' [an-Nahl:68]. And the command directed to the mother of Jesus may be a call from an angel like Gabriel, and it by itself does not signify prophethood nor does it necessitate it.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage defines the essential attributes (sifat daruriyya) of prophets, which the author equates with the conditions (shurut) of prophethood. He states that there are four such attributes, and begins with the first: masculinity (al-dhukura). The author asserts that neither prophethood nor messengership can be for a female. He provides two evidences: first, the observed reality of all prophets and messengers mentioned in the Quran were male; second, the attribute of perfection (kamal) required for prophets is incompatible with femininity. He notes that there is consensus among the majority of Muslims on this condition. Then he addresses a potential objection: the Quran uses the word 'wahy' (revelation) for the mother of Moses and a divine command for the mother of Jesus. He explains that the 'wahy' to the mother of Moses is actually 'ilham' (inspiration), a universal human experience, citing that Allah also uses 'wahy' for bees (an-Nahl:68). Similarly, the command to Mary was an angelic call, not prophethood. Thus these instances do not contradict the requirement of masculinity for prophets.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'wahy' in the Quran always refers to divine revelation given to prophets.
Correction: The author explains that 'wahy' can also mean inspiration (ilham), as seen in the cases of the mother of Moses and bees, and does not necessarily imply prophethood.

Checkpoint
Why does the author mention the revelation (wahy) to the mother of Moses and the command to the mother of Jesus?
A) To prove that women can be prophets.
B) To show that the word 'wahy' can mean inspiration, not necessarily prophethood.
C) To argue that these women were prophets but not messengers.
D) To demonstrate that femininity is not a hindrance to prophecy.

Key Takeaway
Masculinity is an essential attribute of prophethood, supported by historical evidence and the perfection required, and Quranic uses of 'wahy' do not contradict this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author states that 'perfection' (kamal) is incompatible with femininity, yet the Qur'an says men and women are created from the same soul (4:1). Do you see a tension between these two statements? Have you ever felt conflicted when encountering theological conclusions that seem to conflict with verses about human equality? How do you resolve that within yourself?
?
This lesson claims that masculinity is a necessary condition for prophethood based on historical reality and perfection. If you find this difficult to accept, is it because you think the argument is weak, or because it challenges your modern sensibilities? Be honest: does your reaction come more from intellectual scrutiny or from a pre-existing discomfort?
?
The author uses the example of bees receiving 'wahy' to argue that the term can mean inspiration. Will you now pause to check the context before jumping to conclusions?

Trustworthiness (al-Amāna) and Prophetic Sinlessness
Buti defines trustworthiness for prophets and states its implication of sinlessness from lying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of prophetic trustworthiness (al-amāna) and how it entails sinlessness from lying in conveying divine revelation.

Core Idea
Prophetic truthfulness is not optional; it is the foundation of trust in revelation.

In this passage, Buti explains the second essential attribute of prophets: trustworthiness. He connects it directly to truthfulness and divine protection from sin. The argument is simple yet profound: if prophets could lie, their mission would be meaningless. This lesson unpacks that logic and its implications for how we receive prophetic teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Buti defines trustworthiness immediately as truthfulness and protection.
2
Identify the key elements
Find the definition, the proof (why prophets must be trustworthy), and the conclusion about sinlessness from lying.
The proof is that a lying prophet would make the sending futile.
3
Reflect on the proof
Ask yourself: why would a prophet who lies make their mission futile? Think about the purpose of prophethood and the nature of divine wisdom.
This connects to the impossibility of futility (عبث) in Allah's actions.
4
Distinguish the two types of lying
Notice the distinction between deliberate and forgetful lying. Understand the consensus and the majority view.
This distinction is important for understanding the extent of prophetic sinlessness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفة الثانية : الأمانة ونعني بها الصدق وحفظ الله لظواهرهم وبواطنهم عن التلبس بأي منهي عنه ، إذ لو لم يكونوا كذلك لكانت بعثتهم إلى الناس عبثاً ، وهو محال على الله عز وجل كما قد علمت وهذا يعني أن الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام معصومون عن الكذب خصوصاً فيما يتعلق بأمر الشرائع وتبليغ الأحكام وإرشاد الأمة . أما عمداً فبالإجماع ، وأما سهواً فعند جمهور المسلمين .
The second attribute: trustworthiness. And by it we mean truthfulness and Allah's protection of their outward and inward from being tainted by anything forbidden, because if they were not like that, their sending to people would be futile, and that is impossible for Allah, may He be exalted, as you have known. And this means that the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, are sinless regarding lying, especially in matters of the laws, conveying rulings, and guiding the nation. As for deliberately, by consensus; as for forgetfully, according to the majority of Muslims.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage defines the second attribute of prophets: trustworthiness (al-amāna). The author explains that it means truthfulness and divine protection from any sin. The proof is that if prophets could lie, their mission would be pointless, which cannot be attributed to Allah. The author emphasizes that prophets are sinless from lying in matters of religion and guidance. He distinguishes between deliberate lying (sinless by consensus) and forgetful lying (sinless according to the majority).

Correction: The author states that according to the majority, prophets are sinless from lying even forgetfully, especially in matters of religion.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Prophets are divinely protected from lying, especially in conveying revelation, because otherwise their mission would be futile.

?

Consensus on Prophetic Infallibility from Major Sins
Buti states the two certain categories of prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets are infallible from disbelief and major sins before and after prophethood by consensus.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from disbelief and major sins at all times by unanimous agreement.

Before exploring the debate on minor sins, we must first establish what all scholars agree upon. The author begins by affirming that prophets are divinely protected from the two most severe categories of sin: disbelief and major sins. This consensus forms the bedrock of Islamic belief in prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on major sins
Read the Arabic passage that defines the third attribute and states the consensus on disbelief and major sins. Note the emphasis on both before and after prophethood.
The author uses the word 'الإجماع' (consensus) twice for emphasis.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the two categories of sin explicitly mentioned: الكفر (disbelief) and الكبائر (major sins). Notice that the author calls disbelief 'أخطرها' (the most severe).
3
Reflect on the scope of consensus
Ask yourself: Does this consensus apply only after prophethood, or also before? The passage clearly states both.
This is important for understanding the completeness of divine protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفة الثالثة : العصمة عن الوقوع في الذنوب : وفي هذه الصفة تفصيل يجب الوفاء به ، وهو أن الذنوب تختلف في الخطورة . فأما أخطرها وهو الكفر ، فهم معصومون عنه قبل النبوة وبعـدهـا بالإجماع ، وأما تعمد ارتكاب الكبائر فهو أيضاً محال عليهم قبل النبوة وبعـدهـا بالإجماع . وأما الصغائر التي لاتخل بالمروءة ولا تستلزم خسة ، فهي محل خلاف وبحث عند العلماء ، والبحث فيه داخل في الأمور الاجتهادية التي لم تنهض لها أدلة قاطعة تقطع دابر الخلاف فيها ، وإن كان جمهور أهل السنة والجماعة يميلون إلى القول بامتناع الصغائر في حق الأنبياء خصوصاً بعد البعثة ، ومن أجل أننا التزمنا في هذا الكتاب أن لانفصل القول إلا في اليقينيات التي قامت على براهين قاطعة ، مما يكفر جـاحـدهـا - لانرى لزاماً أن نخوض في شيء من الخلافيات الفرعية التي يجوز للمجتهد أن يجنح فيها إلى أكثر من حكم واحد نظراً للأدلة المحتملة ، وحسبك أن تعلم وتعتقد بأن الأنبياء معصومون عن الكفر والكبائر قبل البعثة وبعدها قطعاً ، ومعصومون عن الصغائر فيما ذهب إليه الجمهور .
The third attribute: infallibility from falling into sins. And in this attribute there is a detail that must be fulfilled: that sins vary in severity. As for the most severe, namely disbelief, they are infallible from it before prophethood and after it by consensus. And as for deliberately committing major sins, it is also impossible for them before prophethood and after it by consensus. As for minor sins that do not impair manliness nor entail baseness, they are a matter of disagreement and research among scholars, and the research on it is among the ijtihādī matters for which there are no definitive proofs that cut off the root of disagreement, although the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jamā‘ah incline to say that minor sins are impossible for prophets, especially after the mission. And because we have committed in this book to speak definitively only on certainties based on conclusive proofs, which necessitate takfīr of the denier, we do not see it necessary to delve into subsidiary matters of disagreement in which a mujtahid may lean towards more than one ruling due to probable evidences. It suffices you to know and believe that prophets are infallible from disbelief and major sins before and after prophethood definitively, and infallible from minor sins according to the view of the majority.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses the third attribute: infallibility (al-‘iṣma) from sins. The author divides sins into categories: kufr (disbelief) and kabā’ir (major sins) - prophets are infallible by consensus before and after prophethood. Minor sins (ṣaghā’ir) that do not affect dignity are a subject of scholarly debate, but the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah hold that they are impossible for prophets, especially after their mission. The author notes that his book deals only with definitive matters, so he does not delve into this debate, but affirms that the certain belief is infallibility from kufr and kabā’ir definitively, and from ṣaghā’ir according to the majority.

Key Terms
العصمة
الكفر
الكبائر
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets could commit disbelief or major sins before prophethood, since they were not yet prophets.
Correction: The passage states there is consensus that prophets are infallible from disbelief and major sins both before and after prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when are prophets infallible from major sins?
A) Only after prophethood
B) Before and after prophethood by consensus
C) Only before prophethood
D) Only during their mission

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from disbelief and major sins at all times, a point of absolute consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The prophets were protected from sin – does this humble me or make me feel distant? How can I draw closer to Allah by emulating their purity, especially in my weakest moments?

The Status of Minor Sins and the Author's Approach
Buti discusses the debate on minor sins and his methodological approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that minor sins are a subject of scholarly debate, but the majority view is that prophets are infallible from them, especially after prophethood, and that the author only addresses certainties in this book.

Core Idea
Minor sins are debated, but the majority holds prophets infallible from them.

Having established the certain categories, the author now turns to the debated area: minor sins. He explains the nature of the disagreement, the majority view, and then clarifies why he will not discuss it in depth—because his book only covers definitive certainties. This lesson helps you navigate between what is certain and what is open to ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on minor sins
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the description of minor sins and the position of the majority.
The author describes them as 'لاتخل بالمروءة' (do not impair manliness).
2
Understand the nature of the disagreement
The author says this is a matter of ijtihad, with no definitive proofs. The majority (جمهور أهل السنة) incline to assert infallibility from minor sins, especially after the mission.
3
Reflect on the author's methodology
The author states his book only deals with certainties that necessitate takfir of the denier. He therefore does not delve into the debate, but still affirms the majority view for the reader's belief.
This shows a methodological commitment to avoiding speculative theology.

How can you focus more on what is definitively required?
?
Knowing that prophets are infallible from major sins and from minor sins according to the majority, examine your own heart: Have you ever justified a sin by thinking 'it's only minor' or 'scholars disagree'? How does this lesson challenge you to take every sin seriously and to uphold the prophetic model in all aspects of your life?

Error in ijtihad by prophets is not a sin
Buti clarifies that prophetic error in ijtihad is not a sin and is corrected by revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophetic error in ijtihad is not considered a sin and how it actually strengthens the proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophetic ijtihad error is a proof, not a flaw.

In this passage, Buti addresses a subtle but important point about prophetic infallibility. He argues that when a prophet makes an error in independent reasoning (ijtihad), this is not a sin but an act of worship that gets corrected by revelation. This correction, far from undermining prophethood, becomes one of its strongest proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then consult the translation. Notice the key terms: الخطأ في الاجتهاد, الوحي, التصويب.
The passage is about 8 lines long.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the sentence where Buti states that error in ijtihad is not a sin. Then look for the reason why.
3
Understand the two perspectives
Notice how Buti distinguishes between the error in relation to Allah and the error in relation to the people. This distinction is crucial.
The perspective for the people: they must follow the prophet anyway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الخطأ في الاجتهاد ليس داخلاً في شيء من الذنوب التي ثبتت عصمة الأنبياء عنها إذ الاجتهاد عبادة يثاب عليها المجتهد أصاب أو أخطأ ولكن ثبت أن الأنبياء لا يقرّون على الخطأ في الاجتهاد ، بل لابد أن يأتيهم الوحي ببيان ماهو الأتم والأصوب أو الأكمل في علم الله عز وجل . ومما لا يخفى أن هذا التصويب الذي يأتي به الوحي دليل من أقوى الأدلة على نبوة النبي . وعلى أنها ليست أفكاراً داخلية أو شعوراً وجدانياً كما يتصوره المشككون والمنافقون . وعلى كل فإن خطأ النبي في الاجتهاد لا يسمى خطأ إلا بالنظر لعلاقته . أما بالنظر إلى الناس فلا يسعهم إلا اتباعه في كلا الحالين . أي إن كل ما يأتيهم به النبي صحيح في حقهم يجب قبوله واتباعه .
And know that error in ijtihād is not included in any of the sins from which the infallibility of the prophets is established, because ijtihād is an act of worship for which the mujtahid is rewarded whether he is correct or errs. But it is established that the prophets are not confirmed upon error in ijtihād; rather, revelation must come to them showing what is most perfect, correct, or complete in the knowledge of Allah, may He be exalted. And it is not hidden that this correction brought by revelation is one of the strongest proofs of the prophet's prophethood, and that it is not internal thoughts or emotional feeling as the skeptics and hypocrites imagine. Moreover, the error of the prophet in ijtihād is not called error except in relation to its relation [to Allah]. As for in relation to the people, they have no choice but to follow him in both cases. That is, everything that the prophet brings to them is correct in their regard, and must be accepted and followed.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of prophetic error in ijtihād (independent reasoning). The author argues that such error is not a sin because ijtihād is an act of worship rewarded regardless of correctness. However, prophets are not left in error; revelation corrects them. This correction is a strong proof of prophethood, showing it's not just subjective feeling. The author further explains that from the perspective of the people, whatever the prophet brings is binding and must be followed, even if it was later corrected. The error is only in relation to Allah's ultimate knowledge.

Key Terms
الخطأ في الاجتهاد
الوحي
التصويب
نبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any error by a prophet disproves prophethood.
Correction: Buti explains that error in ijtihad is not a sin and is divinely corrected, which actually proves prophethood is from Allah.

Checkpoint
What does the correction of a prophet's ijtihad error by revelation indicate?
A) That the prophet is fallible like ordinary people
B) That prophethood is proven as divine rather than human invention
C) That the prophet's reasoning is always correct
D) That the prophet can change revelation

Key Takeaway
Prophetic error in ijtihad is not a sin; it is an act of worship corrected by revelation, and this correction is a proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The skeptics and hypocrites dismissed prophethood as 'internal thoughts or emotional feeling.' Do you ever secretly harbor such doubts when you see human imperfections in religious leaders? How does the fact that revelation corrects prophets challenge your own hidden skepticism?

The Fourth Attribute: Perfection of Intellect, Memory, and Justice
Buti defines the fourth attribute and gives a rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth necessary attribute of prophets and why deficiency in these traits would contradict the purpose of prophethood.

Core Idea
A prophet's mission demands perfection of intellect, memory, and justice.

Buti continues defining the essential attributes of prophets. The fourth attribute is not a single trait but a set of three: perfect intellect, perfect memory, and perfect justice. He presents a rational argument showing that any deficiency in these would render the prophetic mission futile, which is impossible for Allah. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition
Read the Arabic passage defining the fourth attribute. Notice the three components: كمال العقل, الضبط, العدالة.
These are listed as a single attribute but have three parts.
2
Understand the rational argument
The passage argues that if a messenger were deficient in these, it would contradict the purpose of the message. Trace the logic: mission requires delivery → delivery requires these qualities → deficiency means contradiction.
This is a proof from reason, not revelation.
3
Reflect on impossibility for Allah
The passage concludes that deficiency would be 'عبث محال' (futile impossible) for Allah. Consider why Allah cannot do futile things.
This is based on divine wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفة الرابعة : كمال العقل والضبط والعدالة : إذ هي من مستلزمات أداء الرسالة التي كلف بتبليغها ، ولو أمكن أن يكون الرسول ناقصاً في عقله أو ضبطه ، أو عدالته مع تكليفه بتبليغ الرسالة المنوطة به ، لكان ذلك متنافياً مع أصل الرسالة ، وهو من العبث المحال على الله عز وجل . واعلم أن هذه الصفات الأربع التي يجب توفرها في الرسول والنبي ، دلّ عليها كل من برهاني السمع والعقل ، أما السمع فما سمعناه في القرآن وصحيح السنة من صفات الرسل والأنبياء الذين بعثوا على مر الأزمنة والدهور ، وأما العقل فما قررناه من استلزام أداء الرسالة الموكولة إليهم ، لهذه الصفات وارتباطه بها . وإذا تبين لك أن هذه هي الشرائط والصفات التي يجب أن تتحقق في الرسل والأنبياء ، أيقنت أنهم ليسوا من وراء ذلك إلا بشراً كسائر الناس ، يأكلون ويشربون وينكحون ويمشون في الأسواق ، وتعتلج في نفوسهم الشهوات الإنسانية كلها ؛ يجوعون فيشتهون الطعام ، ويعطشون فيتوقون إلى الشراب ، ويتعبون فيميلون إلى الراحة ، ويُؤذون فيشعرون بألم الأذى كبقية الناس ، تتعرض قلوبهم
The fourth attribute: perfection of intellect, memory, and justice. For they are among the requirements of performing the message with which he is charged to convey. And if it were possible for the messenger to be deficient in his intellect, memory, or justice, while being charged with conveying the entrusted message, that would be contradictory to the principle of the message, and it is futile, impossible for Allah, may He be exalted. And know that these four attributes that must be present in the messenger and prophet are indicated by both the proofs of transmitted revelation and reason. As for transmitted revelation, it is what we have heard in the Qur'an and sound Sunnah regarding the attributes of the messengers and prophets who were sent throughout the ages and times. As for reason, it is what we have established of the necessity for fulfilling the message entrusted to them to require these attributes and its connection to them. And when it is clear to you that these are the conditions and attributes that must be realized in the messengers and prophets, you will be certain that beyond that they are but human like other people; they eat, drink, marry, walk in the markets, and all human desires stir in their souls; they get hungry and desire food, get thirsty and yearn for drink, get tired and incline to rest, get harmed and feel the pain of harm like the rest of people; their hearts are exposed...
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth attribute: perfection of intellect, memory, and justice. The author argues that these are necessary for delivering the message; deficiency would make the mission futile, which is impossible for Allah. Then he states that all four attributes (trustworthiness, infallibility, perfection of intellect/memory/justice) are proven by both revelation (Qur'an and Sunnah) and reason (rational necessity of the mission). Finally, he emphasizes that aside from these attributes, prophets are fully human, experiencing all human needs and feelings.

الضبط
العدالة
العبث
المحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets could be deficient in intellect or memory as long as they receive revelation.
Correction: Buti argues that any deficiency would contradict the mission, because proper delivery of the message requires these qualities.

Checkpoint

B) It would contradict the principle of the message and be futile.
C) It would only affect his personal life, not his mission.
D) It would be possible but rare.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be perfect in intellect, memory, and justice because any deficiency would make their mission futile, which is impossible for Allah.

Proving the Four Attributes: Revelation and Reason
Buti states that revelation and reason prove the four attributes, and affirms prophets' humanity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the four necessary attributes of prophets are proven by both revelation (Qur'an and Sunnah) and reason, and that prophets remain fully human in other aspects.

Core Idea
Revelation and reason together confirm the prophetic attributes; beyond them, prophets are human.

After establishing the four attributes, Buti now explains that these are not arbitrary but are proven by two independent sources: revelation (سمع) and reason (عقل). He then clarifies an important corollary: aside from these essential attributes, prophets are completely human, experiencing the same physical and emotional needs as everyone else. This lesson examines this dual proof and its implication.

1
Read the passage on proofs
Read the Arabic text that begins with 'واعلم أن هذه الصفات الأربع'. Note the two proofs: السمع and العقل.

2
Compare the two proofs
One proof comes from what we hear in the Qur'an and Sunnah about prophets. The other comes from rational reasoning about the mission's requirements.
Both proofs lead to the same conclusion.
3
Understand the humanity of prophets
The passage emphasizes that beyond these attributes, prophets are 'بشراً كسائر الناس'. Reflect on the examples given: eating, drinking, emotions.
This balances the high status with normal humanity.

The Fourth Attribute of Prophets: Intellect, Accuracy, Justice
Defines the fourth required attribute of prophets and explains its necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must possess complete intellect, accuracy, and justice as necessary attributes for delivering the divine message.

Core Idea
A prophet's mission demands completeness in mind and character.

In this passage, the author introduces the fourth attribute required in prophets: completeness of intellect, accuracy, and justice. He provides a rational argument: delivering a divine message requires a messenger who is fully capable and trustworthy. Any deficiency would make the mission self-contradictory, which cannot be attributed to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the key terms and the structure of the argument.
2
Identify the three qualities

These are essential for trustworthiness.
3
Analyze the rational argument
The author argues that any deficiency in these would contradict the purpose of the message. See how he uses a conditional (لو) to show the impossibility.
The argument is a reduction to absurdity.
4
Reflect on the consequence
Consider why the author equates deficiency with ‘futile impossibility’ regarding Allah. What does this tell us about Allah’s wisdom?
Allah does not do anything in vain.

This passage states the fourth attribute required in prophets: completeness of intellect, accuracy, and justice.
