Farid Wajdi's Denial of Miracles in the Sira
Buti quotes Farid Wajdi's rationalistic methodology for the Sira.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Farid Wajdi's rationalistic approach to the Prophetic biography and why it contradicts traditional Islamic belief in miracles.

Core Idea
Explaining away miracles by natural causes denies the Prophet's signs.

In this lesson, we examine a concrete example of the reformist trend that sought to reinterpret Islamic sources through a rationalistic lens. Farid Wajdi published articles claiming that events in the Prophet's life should not be attributed to miracles if they can be explained by ordinary causes, even if the explanation is forced. This passage shows the rejection of supernatural elements characteristic of that movement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic quote and translation. Notice how Wajdi states his methodology explicitly.
Pay attention to the phrase 'even if with some forced effort.'
2
Understand his argument
He says he avoids excess towards miracles and prefers natural explanations. What does 'forced effort' imply about his commitment?
3
Reflect on implications
If miracles can be explained away, what does that do to the proof of prophethood? How does this contradict traditional Islamic theology?
Miracles are signs from Allah; denying them undermines the message.
4
Connect to broader context
This is part of the reformist trend that tried to harmonize Islam with modern science, often at the cost of essential beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد رأينا كيف بدأ فريد وجدي ينشر سلسلة مقالاته الجريئة التي خرج بها على الناس بعنوان (السيرة المحمدية تحت ضوء العلم والفلسفة) والتي يقول فيها ما نصه: «وقد لاحظ قراؤنا أننا نحرص فيما نكتبه في هذه السيرة على أن لا نسرف في كل ناحية إلى ناحية الإعجاز، ما دام يمكن تعليلها بالأسباب العادية حتى ولو بشيء من التكلف». (۱) انظر مجلة نور الإسلام جـ ٧ المجلد ١١ وما بعده.
For we have seen how Farid Wajdi began publishing his bold series of articles that he presented to the people under the title 'The Prophetic Biography in the Light of Science and Philosophy,' in which he says verbatim: 'Our readers have noted that we are keen, in what we write in this biography, not to go to excess from every direction to the direction of the miraculous, as long as it can be explained by ordinary causes even if with some forced effort.' (1) See the magazine 'Nur al-Islam,' vol. 7, issue 11 and after.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage provides a concrete example of the reformist trend. The author mentions that Farid Wajdi published a series of articles titled 'The Prophetic Biography in the Light of Science and Philosophy.' He quotes Wajdi stating that his approach is to avoid attributing events to miracles whenever possible, preferring natural explanations even if forced. This shows the rejection of supernatural elements characteristic of the reformist movement.

Correction: This methodology denies the miraculous nature of events that are meant to be signs of prophethood, and it goes against the consensus of Muslims. Miracles are part of the proof of prophethood and cannot be reduced to natural causes.

Muhammad Abduh's Deviant Definition of Prophet and Messenger
Buti cites Muhammad Abduh's definition of prophet and messenger that contradicts consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Muhammad Abduh's definition of prophet and messenger contradicts orthodox Islamic teaching by reducing prophethood to innate moral perfection without need for revelation or divine selection.

Core Idea
Abduh's definition exchanges divine revelation for innate human perfection.

In this passage, Buti presents a striking example of theological deviation. Muhammad Abduh, a prominent reformist, redefines the very meaning of prophet and messenger, stripping them of reliance on revelation and divine selection. This lesson examines his definition and why it breaks with the consensus of the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic quote from Abduh and its translation. Notice the key terms: prophet, messenger, fitra (innate disposition).
2
Understand the definition
Abduh says a prophet is innately disposed to truth without thought, and if also innately disposed to call others, he is a messenger. Grasp the two categories.
He distinguishes between a prophet (nabi) and a messenger (rasul) based solely on the presence of an innate call to others.
3
Identify the deviation
Compare this definition with the orthodox view that prophets are chosen by Allah and receive revelation. How does Abduh’s reliance on fitra bypass needed elements like revelation and divine selection?
Orthodox belief holds that prophethood is a gift from Allah through revelation, not a natural human development.
4
Consider the implications
What does this definition imply about the role of revelation, miracles, and the special status of prophets? Why would this be considered a deviation from consensus?
This definition could imply that prophethood is attainable through natural moral cultivation, contradicting the uniqueness of the prophetic role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورأينا كيف يكتب الشيخ محمد عبده في مسائل العقيدة، على طريقة غريبة عجيبة يخرج فيها على إجماع المسلمين وبدهيات العقيدة الإسلامية الصحيحة. وذلك حينما يعرف النبي والرسول في تعليقاته على شرح الجلال الدواني فيقول (أقول: قد يعرف النبي بإنسان فطر على الحق علماً وعملاً، أي بحيث لا يعلم إلا حقاً ولا يعمل إلا حقاً على مقتضى الحكمة وذلك يكون بالفطرة، أي لا يحتاج فيه إلى الفكر والنظر. فإن فطر أيضاً على دعوة بني نوعه إلى ما جبل عليه، فهو رسول أيضاً. وإلا فهو نبي فقط). (۲) تعليقات الشيخ محمد عبده على شرح العقيدة لجلال الدين الدواني ص ٣.
And we saw how Shaykh Muhammad Abduh writes on matters of creed in a strange and wonderful manner, in which he deviates from the consensus of the Muslims and the self-evident truths of the correct Islamic creed. That is when he defines the prophet and the messenger in his commentaries on the commentary of al-Jalal al-Dawwani, saying: 'I say: The prophet may be defined as a human being who is innately disposed to truth in knowledge and action, i.e., such that he knows only truth and acts only truth in accordance with wisdom, and that is by innate disposition (fitra), meaning he does not need thought and reflection. Then if he is also innately disposed to calling his fellow humans to what he is created for, then he is also a messenger. Otherwise, he is only a prophet.' (2) Shaykh Muhammad Abduh's commentaries on the commentary on the creed by Jalal al-Din al-Dawwani, p. 3.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage gives another example of deviant thought. The author states that Muhammad Abduh writes on creed in a strange way, contradicting Muslim consensus and clear truths. He then quotes Abduh's definition: a prophet is a human innately disposed to truth in knowledge and action, without need for thought. If also disposed to call others, he is a messenger. This definition reduces prophethood to natural moral perfection, bypassing the need for revelation and divine selection, which contradicts orthodox Islamic teaching.

Key Terms
النبي
الرسول
الفطرة
الإجماع
البدهيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Abduh's definition is a valid theological definition consistent with Islamic teachings.
Correction: Abduh's definition contradicts the consensus of Muslims and self-evident truths of Islam because it reduces prophethood to natural human perfection and bypasses the necessity of revelation and divine selection.

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad Abduh's definition quoted by Buti, what distinguishes a prophet from a messenger?
A) A prophet is sent to a specific people, a messenger to all.
B) A prophet only knows truth by nature, while a messenger also receives revelation.
C) If the prophet is also innately disposed to call people to what he is created for, he is a messenger; otherwise only a prophet.
D) A prophet performs miracles, a messenger does not.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad Abduh's definition of prophethood based solely on innate disposition contradicts the Islamic belief that prophets are chosen by Allah and receive revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Buti's Critique of Abduh's Definition of Prophet
Buti condemns Abduh's definition of prophet and messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti rejects Muhammad Abduh's definition of prophet and messenger as contrary to Islamic consensus and the proper understanding of prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophet and messenger are not defined by innate disposition but by divine selection and revelation.

In this passage, Buti sharply criticizes the modern scholar Muhammad Abduh for defining a prophet as someone innately disposed to truth, without needing revelation or miracles. Buti considers this definition a departure from the consensus of Muslims and the foundational truths of Islamic creed. Let us examine the definition and Buti's condemnation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Buti opens with a strong condemnation before quoting Abduh.
2
Identify Abduh's definition of prophet and messenger
In the quoted text, find how Abduh defines a prophet (nabi) and how he distinguishes a messenger (rasul).
Note the key term 'fitrah' (innate disposition) and its role in the definition.
3
Understand why Buti calls it deviant
Reflect on Buti's claim that this definition deviates from consensus (ijma) and self-evident truths (badihiyyat). Consider what the traditional definition might be.
This connects to the learning objective: why this definition is problematic.

And we have seen how Sheikh Muhammad Abduh writes on matters of creed in a strange and astonishing manner in which he deviates from the consensus of the Muslims and the self-evident truths of the correct Islamic creed. If he is also innately disposed to calling his fellow humans to what he himself has been molded upon, then he is also a messenger. Otherwise, he is only a prophet.' Commentary
This passage criticizes Muhammad Abduh's definition of prophet (nabi) and messenger (rasul) as deviating from Muslim consensus. Abduh defines a prophet as someone innately (bi’l-fitrah) disposed to truth in knowledge and action, without need for thought or reflection (al-fikr wa’l-nazar). A messenger is one who additionally has an innate disposition to call others. The author marks this as 'strange and astonishing' and contrary to established creed.

Misconception: That a prophet can be defined simply as someone innately disposed to truth without divine selection.
Correction: The traditional Islamic view is that prophethood is a divine gift requiring revelation and miracles, not mere innate disposition.

Key Takeaway
Buti rejects Abduh's definition of prophet and messenger because it replaces divine selection with innate disposition, contradicting Islamic consensus.

Defending the Miraculous: Buti's Critique of Abduh's Tafsir
Buti condemns Abduh's tafsir of the birds and stones as smallpox.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti rejects Muhammad Abduh's interpretation of the birds and stones in Surah al-Fil as a smallpox epidemic, and how this reflects a broader principle about accepting Quranic miracles as literal events.

Core Idea
Literal Quranic miracles cannot be reinterpreted as natural events.

Buti directly criticizes a modern reinterpretation of a well-known miracle story. Muhammad Abduh suggested that the 'birds of ababil' and 'stones of sijjeel' in Surah al-Fil actually referred to a smallpox outbreak. Buti finds this contradicting the clear text and the very idea of Quranic miracles. Let's read his sharp critique and understand its significance.

The question is a refutation by contradiction.
4

And reflect on the clear, unambiguous words of Surat al-Fil, then tell me how it is possible that one who believes in the miracles of the Quran, which are far more extraordinary than the story of the elephant, would deliberately interpret the text of the Quran therein by interpreting the birds of ababil and the stones they threw as smallpox?

The Secular Trend: Replacing Prophethood with Genius and Leadership
Buti critiques Haykal's book and Maraghi's endorsement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a modern revisionist biography of the Prophet, endorsed by a leading Azhar scholar, replaced traditional prophetic attributes with secular concepts like genius and leadership.

Core Idea
Modern biographies can strip prophethood of its divine core.

Buti presents a telling case: a modern biography of the Prophet that claims to use the 'scientific method' and a then-head of Al-Azhar who endorses it by limiting Muhammad's miracle to the Quran as a mental miracle. This lesson explores how such approaches substitute secular praise for the core attributes of prophethood, revelation, and messengership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read Buti's description of Haykal's book and Maraghi's endorsement. Note the exact wording used by both figures.
Observe how Maraghi's phrase 'sound mental miracle' is used.
2
Identify the shift in attributes
Buti lists the attributes that replaced prophethood: 'genius', 'greatness', 'leadership'. Find these in the text and understand what they are replacing.
This is the key point of the critique.
3
Analyze the implications
Consider why Buti sees this as a threat. What happens when prophethood is reduced to human qualities?
Think about the source of authority: divine revelation vs. human intellect.
4
Reflect on the method
Notice Haykal's claim of 'scientific method' ignoring traditional sources. How does this affect credibility?
This ties to broader sectarian issues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورأينا كيف ظهر في تلك الفترة ذاتها كتاب جديد في تحليل السيرة النبوية باسم ( حياة محمد ) للحسين هيكل . يقول في مقدمته ( إنني لم آخذ بما سجلته كتب السيرة والحديث لأنني فضلت أن أجري في هذا البحث على الطريقة العلمية ... ) . ورأينا كيف اندفع الشيخ مصطفى المراغي شيخ الأزهر إذ ذاك إلى تقريظه وتقديمه قائلاً : ( لم تكن معجزة محمد القاهرة إلا في القرآن ، وهي معجزة صالحة عقلية ) . ورأينا كيف أخذت تروُج صفة ( العبقرية ) و ( العظمة ) و ( القيادة ) وما شاكلها للنبي كتعويض عن صفات النبوة والوحي والرسالة ، وتغطية لها وإبعاداً للفكر عنها
And we have seen how in that same period a new book appeared analyzing the Prophetic biography titled 'The Life of Muhammad' by al-Husayn Haykal. He says in its introduction: 'I did not adopt what has been recorded in the books of seerah and hadith because I chose to conduct this research on the scientific method...' And we have seen how Sheikh Mustafa al-Maraghi, the then head of Al-Azhar, rushed to praise and introduce it, saying: 'Muhammad's overwhelming miracle was only in the Quran, and it is a sound mental miracle.' And we have seen how the attributes of 'genius', 'greatness', 'leadership' and the like began to circulate for the Prophet as a substitute for the attributes of prophethood, revelation, and messengership, covering them up and distancing thought from them.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage describes the publication of Husayn Haykal's book 'The Life of Muhammad,' which claims to use the scientific method rather than traditional seerah and hadith. Mustafa al-Maraghi endorsed it, saying that Muhammad's only miracle was the Quran, described as a 'sound mental miracle' (mu‘jiza saliha ‘aqliyya). The author then notes a trend: replacing the attributes of prophethood (nubuwwa), revelation (wahy), and messengership (risala) with secular terms like 'genius' (al-‘abqariyya), 'greatness' (al-‘azama), and 'leadership' (al-qiyada), effectively covering up the true prophetic nature.

Key Terms

القرآن
العبقرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maraghi's endorsement was a balanced, neutral view of the Prophet's miracles.
Correction: Buti shows that Maraghi's statement, by limiting the miracle to a mental one and praising the book that discarded traditional sources, actually contributed to replacing prophetic attributes with secular terms, thus undermining the core of prophethood.

Checkpoint

C) There were no real miracles.

Key Takeaway
When miracles are reduced to mental phenomena and prophetic attributes are replaced by humanistic praise, the divine nature of prophethood is obscured.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Commit to correcting your speech so that you always prioritize his prophethood over any worldly accolade.
?

Do you find yourself rationalizing away miracles because they seem unscientific? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's power? Pledge to affirm miracles without embarrassment, even when they challenge modern sensibilities.

The Objection: Do Quranic Verses Deny Miracles?
Buti presents an objection that Quranic verses deny miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific objection that some Quranic verses appear to deny that prophets bring miracles, and why it seems contradictory.

Core Idea
An objection from the Quran itself seems to undermine the concept of miracles.

Buti anticipates a possible objection from readers familiar with certain Quranic verses. In this lesson, we will examine the objection as it is presented: that verses like 29:50 and 17:90-93 suggest prophets should not bring extraordinary signs. This sets the stage for the answer to come.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a questioner raises a point by quoting two verses.
2
Identify the key verses cited
Find the two Quranic verses: 29:50 and 17:90-93. Understand what each verse says and how it is used to argue against miracles.
The first verse seems to limit signs to God, the second records the Prophet's response to demands for miracles.
3
Understand the logic of the objection
The objector claims that believing in miracles contradicts these clear Quranic texts. See the final question: 'Is not then the assertion of miracles... a contradiction of the clear text?'
This is the core of the objection.
4
Note the tone of the disbelievers' demand
In 17:90-93, the demands are numerous and specific. Notice the polytheists' tone: they are not asking sincerely but testing the Prophet.
Buti will later use this to refute the objection.
5
Prepare to see the answer
The lesson ends with the objection. Think about what might be missing from the objector's interpretation.
The next lesson will provide Buti's refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً ـ المعجزة في ميزان الدين والقرآن :
ثم إنه قد يقول سائل : ولكن في القرآن ما يدل على أن الرسول ليس من شأنه أن يأتي للناس بالخوارق ، كقوله تعالى قل إنّما الآيات عندَ الله وَإِنَّا أَنَا نذير مبين ﴾ [العنكبوت : ٥٠] وقوله تعالى وقالوا لَنْ نُؤْمِنَ لَكَ حَتَّى تَفْجُرَ لَنَا مِنَ الأَرْضِ يَنْبُوعاً أَوْ تَكُونَ لَكَ جَنَّةٌ مِنْ نَخِيلٍ وَعِنَبٍ فَتُفَجِّرَ الأَنْهَارَ خِلالَهَا تَفْجِيراً أَوْ تُسْقِطَ السَّمَاءَ كَمَا زَعَمْتَ عَلَيْنَا كِسَفاً أَوْ تَأْتِيَ بِاللَّهِ وَالْمَلائِكَةِ قَبِيلاً أَوْ يَكُونَ لَكَ بَيْتٌ مِنْ زُخْرُفٍ أَوْ تَرْقَى فِي السَّمَاءِ وَلَنْ نُؤْمِنَ لِرُقِيِّكَ حَتَّى تُنَزِّلَ عَلَيْنَا كِتَاباً نَقْرَؤُهُ قُلْ سُبْحَانَ رَبِّي هَلْ كُنْتُ إِلاَّ بَشَراً رَسُولاً [الإسراء : ۹۰ - ۹۳ ] أفليس القول بالمعجزات والخوارق مع هذا مخالفة لصريح ما في القرآن ؟ والجواب : أن هذه الآيات نزلت قمعاً لسخرية المشركين برسول الله صلعم لا جواباً على سؤال صادق بدر منهم كما ترى من نسق الآيات وأسلوبها . فقد علم الله تعالى أنهم إنما يطالبون بما يقترحونه من الآيات استهزاءً بالنبي عليه الصلاة والسلام وإمعاناً في كفرهم وعنادهم وتعبيراً عن أنهم لا يقبلون رسالة إليهم من الله إلا إذا سلمهم إياها ملك من السماء لا بشر مثلهم في الأرض . ولو علم الله منهم صدق الطلب وحسن النية وأنهم مقبلون في ذلك على محاولة التأكد من صدق النبي صلعم لأعطاهم ما يقنعهم في ذلك . ولكن أمرهم مطابق في ذلك لما وصفه الله تعالى في آية أخرى إذ قال : ﴿ وَلَو فَتَحْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ بَاباً مِنَ السَّمَاءِ فَظَلُّوا فِيهِ يَعْرُجُونَ لَقَالُوا إِنَّمَا سُكِّرَتْ أَبْصَارُنَا بَل نَحْنُ قَوْمٌ مَسْحُورُونَ ﴾ [ الحجر : ١٤-١٥ ]
Third: The miracle in the balance of religion and the Quran: Then a questioner might say: But in the Quran there is what indicates that the messenger is not of such a nature as to bring extraordinary things to people, like His statement Exalted is He: 'Say, the signs are only with God, and I am only a plain warner' [Al-Ankabut: 50] and His statement Exalted is He: 'And they said: We will not believe in you until you cause a spring to gush forth from the earth for us, or you have a garden of palm trees and vines and cause rivers to burst forth in it abundantly, or you cause the sky to fall upon us in pieces as you have claimed, or you bring God and the angels before [us] as a surety, or you have a house of gold, or you ascend into the sky, and we will not believe in your ascension until you send down to us a book we can read. Say: Glorified be my Lord! Am I anything but a human messenger?' [Al-Isra: 90-93] Is not then the assertion of miracles and extraordinary things, despite this, a contradiction of the clear [text] in the Quran? And the answer: That these verses were revealed to suppress the mockery of the polytheists against the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, not as an answer to a sincere question that came from them, as you see from the sequence of the verses and their style. For God Exalted is He knew that they only demanded what they proposed of signs out of mockery of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, and persistence in their disbelief and obstinacy, and as an expression that they do not accept a message to them from God unless an angel from heaven delivers it to them, not a human like themselves on earth. And if God had known from them sincerity of request and good intention and that they were, in that, approaching an attempt to verify the truthfulness of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, He would have given them what would convince them of that. But their matter is in accordance with what God Exalted is He described in another verse when He said: 'And even if We opened to them a gate from the heaven and they continued ascending therein, they would say: Our eyes have only been dazzled; nay, we are a people bewitched.' [Al-Hijr: 14-15]
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer format concerning miracles (muʿjizāt) in the Quran. The objection quotes two verses: Surah Al-Ankabut 29:50, where the Prophet is told to say that signs are only with God, and Surah Al-Isra 17:90-93, where the disbelievers demand specific miracles and the Prophet responds that he is but a human messenger. The objector claims that these verses show prophets are not supposed to bring miracles, so believing in miracles contradicts the Quran. The author, Buti, answers by explaining the context: these verses were revealed to rebuke the mockery (sukhriyya) of the polytheists, not as a genuine denial of miracles. The polytheists were not sincerely seeking proof; they were ridiculing the Prophet. God knew their insincerity, and even if He had given them every sign, they would have dismissed it as sorcery, as the verse from Al-Hijr 15:14-15 illustrates. Therefore, these verses do not negate the possibility of miracles for prophets; they only expose the disbelievers' bad faith. The argument follows the author's own sequence: first the objection is stated, then the answer is given in two parts: (1) the verses were for rebuking mockery, and (2) God's knowledge of their insincerity supports this interpretation.

Key Terms
المعجزة (muʿjiza)
الخوارق (khawāriq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quranic verses like 29:50 and 17:90-93 prove that prophets do not perform miracles.
Correction: These verses were revealed in response to the mockery of disbelievers, not as a universal denial of miracles.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the objection presented in this passage?
A) Prophets should not perform any miracles.
B) Quranic verses seem to deny that prophets bring extraordinary signs.
C) The disbelievers were sincere in asking for miracles.
D) The Prophet refused to perform miracles.

Key Takeaway
The objection uses apparent Quranic texts to argue against miracles, but ignores the context of revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the objection in this lesson, did you feel any doubt about the reality of miracles? What does that reveal about the strength of your conviction in prophethood? This week, pick one of the cited verses (29:50 or 17:90-93) and study its full tafsir to solidify your understanding.
?
The objector uses Quranic verses to argue against miracles. Have you ever encountered someone using a verse to support a false belief? How did you respond? Now, commit to learning the context of any verse before accepting an interpretation that contradicts established aqeedah.
?
If you were to meet a person who sincerely believes this objection, what would you say to them? More importantly, do you yourself fully believe that the Prophet ﷺ performed miracles? Pray to Allah to increase your certainty in the truth of prophethood and the signs given to His messengers.

Buti's Refutation: The Verses Rebuke Mockery
Buti refutes the objection by explaining the context of mockery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's refutation: that the Quranic verses cited in the objection were revealed to suppress mockery, not as a denial of miracles.

Core Idea
The verses rebuke mockery, not the reality of miracles.

Having presented the objection, Buti now provides a decisive answer rooted in the context of revelation. He explains that the verses were a response to the polytheists' mockery, not a theological statement about miracles. This lesson unpacks his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer passage
Read the Arabic passage for the answer, then its translation. Notice that Buti begins with 'And the answer:' directly responding to the objection.
2
Understand the key point: verses were for rebuking mockery
Buti claims the verses were revealed 'to suppress the mockery of the polytheists', not as an answer to a sincere question. This is the heart of his refutation.
The word سخرية (sukhriyya) means mockery.
3
Note the evidence from style and sequence
Buti says you can see this from 'the sequence of the verses and their style'. Look at how the demands escalate and the tone of the polytheists.
This suggests the verses themselves contain clues about the disbelievers' insincerity.
4
See the supporting verse from Al-Hijr
Buti quotes Al-Hijr 15:14-15 to show that even if the disbelievers witnessed a miracle, they would still deny it, claiming sorcery.
This reinforces that their rejection was not due to lack of evidence but sheer obstinacy.
5
Reflect on the principle: sincere seekers would be given signs
Buti states that if God had known sincerity from them, He would have given them convincing signs. This implies that miracles are indeed given to sincere seekers.
This lesson affirms the possibility of miracles for prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً ـ المعجزة في ميزان الدين والقرآن :
ثم إنه قد يقول سائل : ولكن في القرآن ما يدل على أن الرسول ليس من شأنه أن يأتي للناس بالخوارق ، كقوله تعالى قل إنّما الآيات عندَ الله وَإِنَّا أَنَا نذير مبين ﴾ [العنكبوت : ٥٠] وقوله تعالى وقالوا لَنْ نُؤْمِنَ لَكَ حَتَّى تَفْجُرَ لَنَا مِنَ الأَرْضِ يَنْبُوعاً أَوْ تَكُونَ لَكَ جَنَّةٌ مِنْ نَخِيلٍ وَعِنَبٍ فَتُفَجِّرَ الأَنْهَارَ خِلالَهَا تَفْجِيراً أَوْ تُسْقِطَ السَّمَاءَ كَمَا زَعَمْتَ عَلَيْنَا كِسَفاً أَوْ تَأْتِيَ بِاللَّهِ وَالْمَلائِكَةِ قَبِيلاً أَوْ يَكُونَ لَكَ بَيْتٌ مِنْ زُخْرُفٍ أَوْ تَرْقَى فِي السَّمَاءِ وَلَنْ نُؤْمِنَ لِرُقِيِّكَ حَتَّى تُنَزِّلَ عَلَيْنَا كِتَاباً نَقْرَؤُهُ قُلْ سُبْحَانَ رَبِّي هَلْ كُنْتُ إِلاَّ بَشَراً رَسُولاً [الإسراء : ۹۰ - ۹۳ ] أفليس القول بالمعجزات والخوارق مع هذا مخالفة لصريح ما في القرآن ؟ والجواب : أن هذه الآيات نزلت قمعاً لسخرية المشركين برسول الله صلعم لا جواباً على سؤال صادق بدر منهم كما ترى من نسق الآيات وأسلوبها . فقد علم الله تعالى أنهم إنما يطالبون بما يقترحونه من الآيات استهزاءً بالنبي عليه الصلاة والسلام وإمعاناً في كفرهم وعنادهم وتعبيراً عن أنهم لا يقبلون رسالة إليهم من الله إلا إذا سلمهم إياها ملك من السماء لا بشر مثلهم في الأرض . ولو علم الله منهم صدق الطلب وحسن النية وأنهم مقبلون في ذلك على محاولة التأكد من صدق النبي صلعم لأعطاهم ما يقنعهم في ذلك . ولكن أمرهم مطابق في ذلك لما وصفه الله تعالى في آية أخرى إذ قال : ﴿ وَلَو فَتَحْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ بَاباً مِنَ السَّمَاءِ فَظَلُّوا فِيهِ يَعْرُجُونَ لَقَالُوا إِنَّمَا سُكِّرَتْ أَبْصَارُنَا بَل نَحْنُ قَوْمٌ مَسْحُورُونَ ﴾ [ الحجر : ١٤-١٥ ]
Third: The miracle in the balance of religion and the Quran: Then a questioner might say: But in the Quran there is what indicates that the messenger is not of such a nature as to bring extraordinary things to people, like His statement Exalted is He: 'Say, the signs are only with God, and I am only a plain warner' [Al-Ankabut: 50] and His statement Exalted is He: 'And they said: We will not believe in you until you cause a spring to gush forth from the earth for us, or you have a garden of palm trees and vines and cause rivers to burst forth in it abundantly, or you cause the sky to fall upon us in pieces as you have claimed, or you bring God and the angels before [us] as a surety, or you have a house of gold, or you ascend into the sky, and we will not believe in your ascension until you send down to us a book we can read. Say: Glorified be my Lord! Am I anything but a human messenger?' [Al-Isra: 90-93] Is not then the assertion of miracles and extraordinary things, despite this, a contradiction of the clear [text] in the Quran? And the answer: That these verses were revealed to suppress the mockery of the polytheists against the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, not as an answer to a sincere question that came from them, as you see from the sequence of the verses and their style. For God Exalted is He knew that they only demanded what they proposed of signs out of mockery of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, and persistence in their disbelief and obstinacy, and as an expression that they do not accept a message to them from God unless an angel from heaven delivers it to them, not a human like themselves on earth. And if God had known from them sincerity of request and good intention and that they were, in that, approaching an attempt to verify the truthfulness of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, He would have given them what would convince them of that. But their matter is in accordance with what God Exalted is He described in another verse when He said: 'And even if We opened to them a gate from the heaven and they continued ascending therein, they would say: Our eyes have only been dazzled; nay, we are a people bewitched.' [Al-Hijr: 14-15]
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer format concerning miracles (muʿjizāt) in the Quran. The objection quotes two verses: Surah Al-Ankabut 29:50, where the Prophet is told to say that signs are only with God, and Surah Al-Isra 17:90-93, where the disbelievers demand specific miracles and the Prophet responds that he is but a human messenger. The objector claims that these verses show prophets are not supposed to bring miracles, so believing in miracles contradicts the Quran. The author, Buti, answers by explaining the context: these verses were revealed to rebuke the mockery (sukhriyya) of the polytheists, not as a genuine denial of miracles. The polytheists were not sincerely seeking proof; they were ridiculing the Prophet. God knew their insincerity, and even if He had given them every sign, they would have dismissed it as sorcery, as the verse from Al-Hijr 15:14-15 illustrates. Therefore, these verses do not negate the possibility of miracles for prophets; they only expose the disbelievers' bad faith. The argument follows the author's own sequence: first the objection is stated, then the answer is given in two parts: (1) the verses were for rebuking mockery, and (2) God's knowledge of their insincerity supports this interpretation.

Key Terms
المعجزة (muʿjiza)
الخوارق (khawāriq)
السخرية (sukhriyya)
الاستهزاء (istihzāʾ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quranic verses like 29:50 and 17:90-93 prove that prophets do not perform miracles.
Correction: These verses were specifically addressing the mockery of disbelievers and do not deny miracles for sincere seekers.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why did God not give the disbelievers the signs they demanded?
A) Because prophets cannot perform miracles.
B) Because they were insincere and mocking.
C) Because the signs were too difficult.
D) Because the Prophet refused.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verses that appear to deny miracles actually condemn the mockery of disbelievers and affirm that sincere seekers would receive signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek knowledge or ask for a sign from Allah, do you examine your own heart: are you truly sincere (ṣādiq) or are you testing God? Will you continue to reject even if a clear sign comes, like the polytheists who would claim sorcery?
?
Have you ever mocked or dismissed a truth because it came through a fallible human vessel, just as the polytheists demanded an angel instead of a human prophet? What does that reveal about your pride?
?
If God were to give you a miracle right now, would it change your obedience? Or are you like those described in Al-Hijr 15:14-15, whose eyes are 'dazzled' and hearts 'bewitched' by their own arrogance? This lesson forces you to ask: are you in the path of the sincere or the mockers?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Prophethood Is a Divine Choice, Not a Human Craft
Buti concludes that prophethood is divine choice and refutes its evolution from occult arts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophethood is exclusively a divine appointment and not a human invention or evolutionary product.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a divine gift, not a human craft.

In this passage, Buti concludes his earlier arguments by emphasizing that prophethood comes solely by Allah's choice. He then warns against a common misconception that views prophethood as a refined version of ancient occult practices. This lesson will unpack his reasoning and the decisive barrier he erects between divine revelation and human speculation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Buti connects this issue to his previous four discussions.
The passage begins with 'This last issue is a clear result...'
2
Identify the Quranic Proofs
Find the two Quranic verses Buti cites (Quran 6:124 and 22:75). Understand how they support the idea that prophethood is by Allah's choice alone.
3
Understand the False Evolutionary Model
Buti describes how some people imagine prophethood evolved from soothsaying to astrology to magic to prophethood. List these stages: kihana → tanjim → sihr → nubuwwa.
This is the false conception he refutes.
4
Contrast Divine Choice with Human Craft
Buti emphasizes a 'strong scientific barrier' between the true meaning of prophethood (based on revelation and miracles) and the false notion of prophethood as a craft. Reflect on why this distinction matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذه المسألة الأخيرة ، هي في الحقيقة نتيجة واضحة للمسائل الأربع السابقة . فإذا كان أساس النبوة الوحي الذي عرفت معناه ، وإذا كانت المعجزة من المؤيدات التي يؤيد الله بها الأنبياء بقدرته وإرادته - فمعنى ذلك أن الرسالة لا تأتي إلا بمحض اختيار من الله عز وجل ، كما قال في محكم تبيانه : والله أعلم حيثُ يَجْعَلُ رِسالَتَهُ ﴾ [الأنعام : ١٢٤ ] وكما قال في آية أخرى اللهُ يَصطفي مِنَ الملائِكَةِ رُسُلاً وَمِنَ النَّاسِ .. ﴾ [ الحج : ٧٥]
ولكننا مع ذلك آثرنا أن نفرد بحثاً تحت هذا العنوان . وذلك حتى ننبه القارئ إلى الحاجز العلمي الحصين بين معنى ( النبوة ) في الواقع الذي دل عليه العلم والعقل ، بعد أن دل كل منهما على وجود الله عز وجل ، وبين معناها القائم في أوهام أولئك الذي لا يزالون يتخيلون أن النبوة صنعة قائمة بذاتها في سوق الإشراق أو الكهانة والسحر والتنجيم : فهي من صناعات تلك السوق ، إلا أنها الدقة تمتاز عنها بمزيد من
فلا يزال يذهب بعض الناس إلى أن الكهانة كانت في التاريخ الغابر هي الصناعة المقدسة في الحياة ، ثم إنها ترقت مع رقي العقل البشري فتحولت إلى تنجيم ، ثم ازدادت رقياً مع التقدم العلمي والعقلي فانقلبت إلى سحر ، ثم إنهـا وصلت إلى قمة أدوارها التحسينية عندما ظهرت بمظهر النبوة التي تنسكب على قلوب أصحابها في محاريب الخلوة والإشراق الروحي ! أما كيف توالدت هذه الحلقات بعضها من بعض وما هو النسب الذي يصل كل حلقة منها بالأخرى
This last issue is, in fact, a clear result of the four preceding issues. For if the basis of prophethood (nubuwwa) is revelation (wahy), whose meaning you have understood, and if the miracle (mu'jiza) is one of the supports by which Allah supports the prophets with His power and will, then the meaning is that the message (risala) comes only by pure choice from Allah Almighty, as He said in His clear statement: 'Allah knows best where to place His message' [al-An'am: 124] and as He said in another verse: 'Allah chooses messengers from the angels and from the people...' [al-Hajj: 75].
Nevertheless, we have preferred to devote a discussion under this title, so that we may alert the reader to the strong scientific barrier between the meaning of prophethood (nubuwwa) in reality — which has been indicated by knowledge and reason, after each of them has indicated the existence of Allah Almighty — and its meaning that is established in the fantasies of those who still imagine that prophethood is an independent craft in the marketplace of illumination (ishraq) or soothsaying (kihana), magic (sihr), and astrology (tanjim): it is one of the crafts of that marketplace, except that it is distinguished from them by more precision (al-diqqa).
For some people still go so far as to think that soothsaying (kihana) was, in ancient history, the sacred profession in life; then it progressed with the advancement of the human mind and turned into astrology (tanjim); then it increased in progress with scientific and rational development and transformed into magic (sihr); then it reached the peak of its perfective stages when it appeared in the form of prophethood (nubuwwa) that pours into the hearts of its practitioners in the prayer niches of seclusion and spiritual illumination! But how these circles generated one from another and what is the lineage that connects each circle to the other...
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a concluding argument and a warning. The author states that the issue of prophethood being by divine choice is a clear result of the previous four issues. He recaps: if revelation is the basis of prophethood, and miracles are divine supports, then the message comes only by Allah's pure choice, citing Quran 6:124 and 22:75. He then explains why he has devoted a separate discussion: to draw a sharp line between the true meaning of prophethood (established by knowledge and reason after proving God's existence) and the false conception held by those who imagine prophethood as a human craft in the marketplace of 'illumination' (ishraq), soothsaying (kihana), magic (sihr), and astrology (tanjim). They think prophethood is just a refined version of these ancient arts. He notes that some people believe that kihana was the original sacred profession, which evolved into astrology, then into magic, and finally into prophethood as its perfected form — as if prophethood were a human invention. The passage breaks off at the point where it would explain how these circles are related, due to the page ending. The author's intent is to refute the notion that prophethood is a product of human development, emphasizing instead that it is a pure divine gift.

Key Terms
نبوة (nubuwwa)
وحي (wahy)
معجزة (mu'jiza)
إشراق (ishraq)
كهانة (kihana)
سحر (sihr)
تنجيم (tanjim)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood is a human invention that evolved from primitive superstitions like soothsaying, astrology, and magic.
Correction: Prophethood is a divine appointment based on revelation and miracles, not a product of human cultural evolution.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the basis for prophethood?
A) A long evolution of human crafts like soothsaying.
B) Revelation (wahy) and divine choice.
C) Spiritual illumination achieved by personal effort.
D) Mastery of occult sciences.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is a divine choice, not a human invention; any theory that links it to occult arts is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek closeness to Allah through worship, do you ever find yourself treating spiritual insight as a skill you can master, forgetting that true guidance is a gift from Allah alone? How does this passage challenge that tendency?
?
Have you ever looked at the lives of the prophets and felt that their station was something you could attain through rigorous spiritual practice, rather than as a pure choice from Allah? What would it mean for you to fully accept that prophethood is exclusively His decision?
?
The source says prophethood is not a craft in the marketplace of illumination – where in your own heart do you try to 'craft' your relationship with Allah, instead of humbly receiving it from Him? What concrete step can you take today to surrender that area to His choice?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Divine Origin of Prophethood
Buti asserts prophethood is by divine choice and contrasts it with false conceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's logical argument that prophethood is a divine selection, not a human attainment, based on the nature of revelation and miracles.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a divine gift, not a human achievement.

Buti begins by recalling the previous discussions on revelation and miracles, which logically lead to the conclusion that prophethood comes solely by God's choice. He supports this with Quranic verses and then explains why he devotes a separate section: to draw a clear line between true prophethood and false notions that confuse it with occult practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening argument
Read the first part of the passage where Buti connects this issue to the previous four. Notice how he uses the established understandings of revelation and miracle to deduce that prophethood is by God's choice alone.
This is a logical deduction, not a new claim.
2
Reflect on the Quranic verses
Buti quotes two verses affirming that God chooses where to place His message and that He selects messengers. Consider how these verses support the previous logical conclusion.
3
Understand the purpose of the section
Buti states he devoted a separate discussion to alert the reader to the barrier between true prophethood and false conceptions. Identify what those false conceptions are (divination, sorcery, astrology).
This prepares for the critique in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خامسًا: النبوة لا تأتي عن طريق الكتب. هذه المسألة الأخيرة، هي في الحقيقة نتيجة واضحة للمسائل الأربع السابقة. فإذا كان أساس النبوة الوحي الذي عرفت معناه، وإذا كانت المعجزة من المؤيدات التي يؤيد الله بها الأنبياء بقدرته وإرادته - فمعنى ذلك أن الرسالة لا تأتي إلا بمحض اختيار من الله عز وجل، كما قال في محكم تبيانه: ﴿ والله أعلم حيثُ يَجْعَلُ رِسالَتَهُ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٢٤] وكما قال في آية أخرى: ﴿ اللهُ يَصطفي مِنَ الملائِكَةِ رُسُلاً وَمِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ [الحج: ٧٥]. ولكننا مع ذلك آثرنا أن نفرد بحثاً تحت هذا العنوان. وذلك حتى ننبه القارئ إلى الحاجز العلمي الحصين بين معنى (النبوة) في الواقع الذي دل عليه العلم والعقل، بعد أن دل كل منهما على وجود الله عز وجل، وبين معناها القائم في أوهام أولئك الذين لا يزالون يتخيلون أن النبوة صنعة قائمة بذاتها في سوق الإشراق أو الكهانة والسحر والتنجيم: فهي من صناعات تلك السوق، إلا أنها تمتاز عنها بمزيد من الدقة. فلا يزال يذهب بعض الناس إلى أن الكهانة كانت في التاريخ الغابر هي الصناعة المقدسة في الحياة، ثم إنها ترقت مع رقي العقل البشري فتحولت إلى تنجيم، ثم ازدادت رقياً مع التقدم العلمي والعقلي فانقلبت إلى سحر، ثم إنها وصلت إلى قمة أدوارها التحسينية عندما ظهرت بمظهر النبوة التي تنسكب على قلوب أصحابها في محاريب الخلوة والإشراق الروحي! أما كيف توالدت هذه الحلقات بعضها من بعض وما هو النسب الذي يصل كل حلقة منها بالأخرى وما برهان ذلك في التاريخ والبحث العلمي، فشيء آخر لم يذهب إليه هؤلاء الناس ولم يبحثوه!!. وطبيعي أن تكون النبوة في تصوير هؤلاء الناس، غاية يتوصل إليها بالسعي والكسب، كما توصل السحرة إلى السحر بالسعي والكسب. وهؤلاء الناس، إن فهموا نبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام، فإنهم لا يفهمونها إلا على هذا الأساس: جهد بذله الرسول سعاه حتى أصبح بذلك نبياً. والنبوة في أوهام هؤلاء رديف تام لكلمة «مصلح» التي كثيراً ما تتردد على ألسنتهم، وهم في هذا إنما يخدعون نفوسهم قبل أن يخدعوا أحداً سواهم. وهم من أجل ذلك، لا يحبون أن يصدقوا أن القرآن كلام غير النبي، ولا يريدون أن يفهموا أنه قد أوتي معجزة جرت على يده، ولا يودون أن يفهموا عن الوحي إلا أنه الفكر والتأمل... وذلك كي يسلم لهم تصور أن النبوة معنى اكتسابي. وقد لا يكون ذلك مفهوماً لديهم من حيث التحليل القابل للتصور، ولكن حسبه على كل أن يكون موصوفاً في تصورهم بأنه كسبي. ونحن بعد أن اجتزنا البحث عن ظاهرة الوحي وما كشف عنها البحث العلمي، واجتزنا بعد ذلك البحث في المعجزة وما كشف عنها البرهان العلمي، واجتزنا قبل ذلك الحديث عن واجب الوجود جل جلاله وما كشف البرهان اليقيني - لا يسعنا إلا أن نستيقن ما ينتجه الحق الذي ظهر لنا في تلك المسائل كلها، ألا وهو أن النبوة ليست إلا وحياً من الله لمن شاء من عباده لينذر الناس يوم التلاق، وليذكرهم بما ذكر به أسلافهم من قبل مما سيلاقونه من بعد يوم الموت، وما يترتب عليهم من الحقوق لخالقهم جل جلاله. فليس لها أي شأن بالكهانة أو السحر أو التنجيم، وليست مما يسعى إليه الناس بالحيلة والجهد.
Fifth: Prophethood does not come through books. This last issue is, in reality, a clear result of the previous four issues. For if the basis of prophethood is revelation—the meaning of which you have understood—and if the miracle is among the supports by which God supports the prophets by His power and will, then that means that the message comes only by mere choice from God Almighty, as He said in His clear revelation: 'And God knows best where to place His message' [Al-An'am 6:124] and as He said in another verse: 'God chooses messengers from the angels and from the people' [Al-Hajj 22:75]. Nevertheless, we have chosen to devote a discussion under this title. This is to alert the reader to the firm scientific barrier between the meaning of 'prophethood' in reality—as indicated by science and reason, after both have indicated the existence of God Almighty—and its meaning present in the delusions of those who still imagine that prophethood is an independent craft in the market of illumination or divination, sorcery, and astrology: it is one of the industries of that market, except that it is distinguished by more precision. Some people still think that divination in ancient history was the sacred industry in life, then it progressed with the advancement of human reason and turned into astrology, then it increased in sophistication with scientific and intellectual progress and turned into sorcery, then it reached the peak of its improvement when it appeared in the form of prophethood that pours into the hearts of its people in the alcoves of seclusion and spiritual illumination! But how these rings evolved from one another and what is the lineage connecting each ring to the other and what is the proof of that in history and scientific research—that is something else that these people have not considered nor investigated!! Naturally, prophecy in the depiction of these people is a goal attained through effort and acquisition, just as sorcerers attain sorcery through effort and acquisition. These people, if they understand the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him), they only understand it on this basis: an effort made by the Messenger that he pursued until he became a prophet by that. Prophethood in the delusions of these people is a complete synonym for the word 'reformer' that often recurs on their tongues, and in this they only deceive themselves before they deceive anyone else. For that reason, they do not like to believe that the Quran is the speech of other than the Prophet, nor do they want to understand that he was given a miracle that occurred at his hand, nor do they wish to understand revelation except as thought and reflection... so that they can maintain their conception that prophethood is an acquired concept. It may not be comprehensible to them in terms of conceivable analysis, but it suffices, after all, that it is described in their conception as acquired. After we have passed through the research on the phenomenon of revelation and what scientific research has revealed, and after that we passed through the research on the miracle and what scientific proof has revealed, and before that we passed through the discourse on the Necessary Existence (majestic is His glory) and what certain proof has revealed—we cannot but be certain of what the truth that has appeared to us in all these issues produces, namely that prophethood is nothing but revelation from God to whomever He wills among His servants to warn people on the Day of Meeting, and to remind them of what He reminded their predecessors before of what they will encounter after the Day of Death, and of the rights they owe to their Creator (majestic is His glory). So it has no connection to divination, sorcery, or astrology, nor is it something people seek by trickery and effort.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a conclusive argument demonstrating that prophethood is a purely divine gift, not a human attainment. The author begins by stating that this issue is the clear result of the previous four discussions on revelation, miracles, and divine existence. If revelation is the basis of prophethood and miracles are divine confirmations, then prophethood must come solely by God's choice—supported by Quranic verses. The author then explains why he devotes a separate section: to draw a sharp distinction between the true meaning of prophethood (as known through reason and science pointing to God) and the false conception held by those who imagine it as a craft in the market of illumination, divination, sorcery, and astrology. He then describes a common false evolution: from divination to astrology to sorcery to prophethood, but notes that those who claim this offer no proof. He further explains that such people view prophethood as a goal attained by effort, akin to how sorcerers acquire sorcery, and that they even interpret the prophethood of Muhammad (PBUH) as a result of his own exertion—thus reducing prophethood to mere reformism. They resist accepting the Quran as divine speech or miracles as supernatural, instead reducing revelation to reflection and thought, all to preserve their acquisition-based view. Finally, the author concludes that after establishing revelation, miracles, and divine existence through certain proofs, we must affirm that prophethood is solely revelation from God to chosen servants for the purpose of warning and reminding. It has nothing to do with divination, sorcery, or astrology, nor is it something sought by human effort.

A) Historical evolution of religion
B) The previous discussions on revelation and miracle

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever secretly believed that you could earn God’s favor or a high spiritual status through your own efforts, like learning a skill? How does Buti’s assertion that prophethood is purely God’s choice—not a human craft—expose that pride in your heart? What will you do today to consciously acknowledge your absolute dependence on God’s selection?
?
This passage draws a 'firm scientific barrier' between the truth of prophethood and the delusions of those who imagine it as divination. Where in your own life have you blurred the line between relying on God and relying on your own intellect, culture, or spiritual practices? Will you let this barrier reshape how you seek guidance from God?
?
Buti quotes two verses to prove that God alone places His message and chooses His messengers. If you truly believe this, then why do you sometimes look to human systems—like self-help, philosophy, or even religious figures—as the ultimate source of truth, rather than submitting to God's revealed word? Commit to one concrete change in how you prioritize the Quran and Sunnah over human opinions today.

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Refuting the Acquisition Model of Prophethood
Buti refutes the acquisition model and reaffirms prophethood as divine revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's refutation of the false evolutionary view that reduces prophethood to an acquired skill, and his reaffirmation that prophethood is purely revelation.

Core Idea
Prophethood is not a product of human effort or historical evolution.

In this continuation, Buti critiques those who imagine prophethood as the final stage of an evolution from divination to sorcery. He exposes the flaw in their reasoning and shows how they reduce prophethood to mere reformism. Then, based on the prior certain proofs, he concludes that prophethood is nothing but revelation from God.

Guided Path
1
Examine the false evolutionary narrative
Buti describes a common false view: divination progressed to astrology, then to sorcery, and finally to prophethood. Note that he points out the lack of evidence for this alleged lineage.
This narrative implies prophethood is a human invention.
2
Understand the acquisition view
Those who hold this narrative see prophethood as a goal attained through effort, just like sorcery. Buti points out that they even reinterpret the prophethood of Muhammad (PBUH) as a result of his own exertion, reducing it to mere reformism.
This leads to denying the divine origin of the Quran and miracles.
3
Grasp the final conclusion
After recalling the certain proofs from previous discussions (revelation, miracle, divine existence), Buti concludes that prophethood is solely revelation from God, for warning and reminding, and has nothing to do with occult practices or human effort.
This is the definitive statement based on earlier certainties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خامسًا: النبوة لا تأتي عن طريق الكتب. هذه المسألة الأخيرة، هي في الحقيقة نتيجة واضحة للمسائل الأربع السابقة. فإذا كان أساس النبوة الوحي الذي عرفت معناه، وإذا كانت المعجزة من المؤيدات التي يؤيد الله بها الأنبياء بقدرته وإرادته - فمعنى ذلك أن الرسالة لا تأتي إلا بمحض اختيار من الله عز وجل، كما قال في محكم تبيانه: ﴿ والله أعلم حيثُ يَجْعَلُ رِسالَتَهُ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٢٤] وكما قال في آية أخرى: ﴿ اللهُ يَصطفي مِنَ الملائِكَةِ رُسُلاً وَمِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ [الحج: ٧٥]. ولكننا مع ذلك آثرنا أن نفرد بحثاً تحت هذا العنوان. وذلك حتى ننبه القارئ إلى الحاجز العلمي الحصين بين معنى (النبوة) في الواقع الذي دل عليه العلم والعقل، بعد أن دل كل منهما على وجود الله عز وجل، وبين معناها القائم في أوهام أولئك الذين لا يزالون يتخيلون أن النبوة صنعة قائمة بذاتها في سوق الإشراق أو الكهانة والسحر والتنجيم: فهي من صناعات تلك السوق، إلا أنها تمتاز عنها بمزيد من الدقة. فلا يزال يذهب بعض الناس إلى أن الكهانة كانت في التاريخ الغابر هي الصناعة المقدسة في الحياة، ثم إنها ترقت مع رقي العقل البشري فتحولت إلى تنجيم، ثم ازدادت رقياً مع التقدم العلمي والعقلي فانقلبت إلى سحر، ثم إنها وصلت إلى قمة أدوارها التحسينية عندما ظهرت بمظهر النبوة التي تنسكب على قلوب أصحابها في محاريب الخلوة والإشراق الروحي! أما كيف توالدت هذه الحلقات بعضها من بعض وما هو النسب الذي يصل كل حلقة منها بالأخرى وما برهان ذلك في التاريخ والبحث العلمي، فشيء آخر لم يذهب إليه هؤلاء الناس ولم يبحثوه!!. وطبيعي أن تكون النبوة في تصوير هؤلاء الناس، غاية يتوصل إليها بالسعي والكسب، كما توصل السحرة إلى السحر بالسعي والكسب. وهؤلاء الناس، إن فهموا نبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام، فإنهم لا يفهمونها إلا على هذا الأساس: جهد بذله الرسول سعاه حتى أصبح بذلك نبياً. والنبوة في أوهام هؤلاء رديف تام لكلمة «مصلح» التي كثيراً ما تتردد على ألسنتهم، وهم في هذا إنما يخدعون نفوسهم قبل أن يخدعوا أحداً سواهم. وهم من أجل ذلك، لا يحبون أن يصدقوا أن القرآن كلام غير النبي، ولا يريدون أن يفهموا أنه قد أوتي معجزة جرت على يده، ولا يودون أن يفهموا عن الوحي إلا أنه الفكر والتأمل... وذلك كي يسلم لهم تصور أن النبوة معنى اكتسابي. وقد لا يكون ذلك مفهوماً لديهم من حيث التحليل القابل للتصور، ولكن حسبه على كل أن يكون موصوفاً في تصورهم بأنه كسبي. ونحن بعد أن اجتزنا البحث عن ظاهرة الوحي وما كشف عنها البحث العلمي، واجتزنا بعد ذلك البحث في المعجزة وما كشف عنها البرهان العلمي، واجتزنا قبل ذلك الحديث عن واجب الوجود جل جلاله وما كشف البرهان اليقيني - لا يسعنا إلا أن نستيقن ما ينتجه الحق الذي ظهر لنا في تلك المسائل كلها، ألا وهو أن النبوة ليست إلا وحياً من الله لمن شاء من عباده لينذر الناس يوم التلاق، وليذكرهم بما ذكر به أسلافهم من قبل مما سيلاقونه من بعد يوم الموت، وما يترتب عليهم من الحقوق لخالقهم جل جلاله. فليس لها أي شأن بالكهانة أو السحر أو التنجيم، وليست مما يسعى إليه الناس بالحيلة والجهد.
Fifth: Prophethood does not come through books. This last issue is, in reality, a clear result of the previous four issues. For if the basis of prophethood is revelation—the meaning of which you have understood—and if the miracle is among the supports by which God supports the prophets by His power and will, then that means that the message comes only by mere choice from God Almighty, as He said in His clear revelation: 'And God knows best where to place His message' [Al-An'am 6:124] and as He said in another verse: 'God chooses messengers from the angels and from the people' [Al-Hajj 22:75]. Nevertheless, we have chosen to devote a discussion under this title. This is to alert the reader to the firm scientific barrier between the meaning of 'prophethood' in reality—as indicated by science and reason, after both have indicated the existence of God Almighty—and its meaning present in the delusions of those who still imagine that prophethood is an independent craft in the market of illumination or divination, sorcery, and astrology: it is one of the industries of that market, except that it is distinguished by more precision. Some people still think that divination in ancient history was the sacred industry in life, then it progressed with the advancement of human reason and turned into astrology, then it increased in sophistication with scientific and intellectual progress and turned into sorcery, then it reached the peak of its improvement when it appeared in the form of prophethood that pours into the hearts of its people in the alcoves of seclusion and spiritual illumination! But how these rings evolved from one another and what is the lineage connecting each ring to the other and what is the proof of that in history and scientific research—that is something else that these people have not considered nor investigated!! Naturally, prophecy in the depiction of these people is a goal attained through effort and acquisition, just as sorcerers attain sorcery through effort and acquisition. These people, if they understand the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him), they only understand it on this basis: an effort made by the Messenger that he pursued until he became a prophet by that. Prophethood in the delusions of these people is a complete synonym for the word 'reformer' that often recurs on their tongues, and in this they only deceive themselves before they deceive anyone else. For that reason, they do not like to believe that the Quran is the speech of other than the Prophet, nor do they want to understand that he was given a miracle that occurred at his hand, nor do they wish to understand revelation except as thought and reflection... so that they can maintain their conception that prophethood is an acquired concept. It may not be comprehensible to them in terms of conceivable analysis, but it suffices, after all, that it is described in their conception as acquired. After we have passed through the research on the phenomenon of revelation and what scientific research has revealed, and after that we passed through the research on the miracle and what scientific proof has revealed, and before that we passed through the discourse on the Necessary Existence (majestic is His glory) and what certain proof has revealed—we cannot but be certain of what the truth that has appeared to us in all these issues produces, namely that prophethood is nothing but revelation from God to whomever He wills among His servants to warn people on the Day of Meeting, and to remind them of what He reminded their predecessors before of what they will encounter after the Day of Death, and of the rights they owe to their Creator (majestic is His glory). So it has no connection to divination, sorcery, or astrology, nor is it something people seek by trickery and effort.
Source pages p. 236

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What is one thought you must fight tonight to uproot this feeling of entitlement from your heart?

What step will you take today to reinforce that the Quran is divine speech?
?

Has your life reflected this truth, or have you—like the people Buti criticizes—tried to turn Islam into a human reform movement, relying on your own intellect and plans instead of submitting to divine guidance? What is one area of your life where you need to stop 'acquiring' and start receiving from Allah? Commit to one concrete change in the next 24 hours.
